<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="broad-objective">BROAD OBJECTIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#broad-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of 24hrs, the learner will have acquired knowledge, skill &amp; attitude to plan, organize, coordinate, implement, monitor &amp; evaluate immunization programme.</p>
<p><strong>SPECIFIC OBJECTIVES</strong>: the learner should be able to;</p>
<ul>
<li>Implement immunization policies, operations, policies, norms &amp; standards</li>
<li>Participate in various immunization delivery services</li>
<li>Manage the delivery types of vaccines</li>
<li>Provide immunization services</li>
<li>Manage an immunization programme.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="content">CONTENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Vaccinology &amp; EPI vaccines-2hrs</strong>;
immunity, immunogenicity, antigen, antibody, natural history of disease, types of immunity, natural (active &amp; passive) artificial (active &amp; passive) &amp; herd, types of vaccines; monovalent, bivalent, combined, live &amp; killed, viral &amp; bacterial, liquid and lymphosized,atics of ideal vaccine, vaccines used in the national imm. schedule. &amp; non-EPI antigens.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Immunization systems &amp; operations-2hrs</strong>;
Introduction to EPI-background, current immunization Kenyan status, immunization operational components.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Def. of terms; combined vaccine coverage, dropout rate, indicator, logistics, norms, missed opportunity vs drop out, supportive supervision,</p>
<p><strong>Policies, norms &amp; stds</strong>; global, African &amp; country, community participation/importance, intergrated approach, accessibility &amp; equity, quality of services &amp; safety, coordination &amp; leadership, regulatory issues related to immunizations.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li><strong>Immunization service delivery &amp; vaccine administration-6+2hrs</strong>;
Routine &amp; national immunization schedules, diluents &amp; reconstitution of vaccines, immunization target groups, cold chain, vaccine mx (cold chain system), cold chain equipment-fridge, cold box, icepacks, vaccine carrier, monitoring refrigerator temps-thermometer, fridge tag, handling cold chain emergencies, H/workers tasks for cold chain management; logistics, procurement, ordering, storage of vaccines &amp; equipments.</li>
</ol>
<p>vaccine tests; shake test, VVM, vaccines arrangement in the fridge.</p>
<p>vit A supplementation &amp; Deworming,</p>
<p>contraindications of immunizations (True/false), HIV &amp; immunizations,</p>
<p>Multi dose vial policy- on opened vials of vaccines,</p>
<p>immunization safety: safe injection practices and disposals-safety boxes, wastes disposal, vaccine quality-</p>
<p>Adverse Events Following immunizations (AEFIs)-def, causes, mx, prevention &amp; reporting.</p>
<p>Surveillance/notification-def, types, epi diseases for elimination and eradication,</p>
<p>organizing &amp; conducting an immunization session, missed opportunities in immunizations-def, causes &amp; prevention. communication of immunization program- roles of communicator/community.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li><strong>Service delivery strategies and innovative approaches-2+2hrs</strong>.</li>
</ol>

<p>Static/fixed, outreach, mobile teams, immunization campaigns, supplemental immunization activities. Strategy for intergretion (Mother&amp;child care) / importance.</p>
<p>Innovative approaches - decade of vaccines, Global vaccine action plan (GVAP) 2011-2020, GVAPD (pneumonia&amp;diarrhea), Reach Every District or Child or Community (RED) approach. New challenges - unimmunized, under immunized, unreached, hard to reach.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-management-of-an-immunization-programme-6hrs">5. Management of an immunization programme - 6hrs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-management-of-an-immunization-programme-6hrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Problem solving approach &amp; role of EPI manager, planning immunization activities, financial &amp; sustainability, supervision by programme manager (role of supervision, supervision styles, monitoring of an immunization programme, implementation, coverage &amp; drop out, data mx &amp; analysis, evaluation programme purpose of evaluation, steps for conducting an evaluation.</p>
<p>Teaching strategies - lectures, group discussions, demonstration, field strips.</p>
<p>Evaluation - exam (PE), FQE &amp; assessment (Rurals)</p>
<p>References: MOH, Kenya (2015) immunization manual for health workers. MOH, Kenya (2015) immunization manual for medical and nursing students. WHO (2015) EPI prototype curriculum (USAID, UNICEF, GAVI)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terminologies-used-in-immunology">Terminologies used in immunology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies-used-in-immunology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Immunity - ability to resist infections or protection against infectious disease</p>
<p>Immunology - science dealing with study of immune system.</p>
<p>Vaccinology - Field of science dealing with studies of vaccines.</p>
<p>Vaccination: The process of administering a vaccine (antigen) or manipulation of the immune system to induce protective immunity against specific disease.</p>
<p>Aimed at reducing morbidity and mortality rates related to prevented infectious diseases.</p>
<p>Vaccine - antigen containing MOs in a weakened or killed state of proteins or toxins from organism.</p>
<p>Immunization - process by which a person immune system is made resistant to specific infections/diseases.</p>
<p>Antigen: antibody generator or any substance, usually a protein that is capable of eliciting an immune response by binding with antibodies and effector cells lymphocytes produced.</p>
<p>The antigens that can cause a disease are called pathogens.</p>
<p>Antibody or immunoglobulin (IGs) - y globulins produced in response to antigen stimulation or a protein produced by plasma cells in response to an antigen eg IgA, M, D, G, E</p>
<p>Immunogenicity: The inherent ability of an antigen to induce an immune response.</p>
<p>Pathogen - disease causing organism</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Opportunistic pathogen-cause diseases in immunosuppressed patients like HIV/AIDS</p>
<p>Virulence- Degree of pathogenicity within a group or species of microorganisms.</p>
<p>Pathogenicity –ability of microorganism to cause infection or disease.</p>
<p>Seroconversion: When an individual following a disease or vaccination generates antigen-specific antibodies.</p>
<p>Vaccine adjuvant: Substance that is added to a vaccine to its immunogenicity without having any specific antigenic effect in itself. These may include mineral salts (aluminium and calcium phosphate), organic adjuvants, particulate adjuvants, virosomes, microbial derivatives, oil emulsions and surfactant based formulations</p>
<p>Incubation period: the interval between exposure to an infectious agent and onset of clinical symptoms. The incubation period varies for different diseases from a few hours to several months or even longer for some diseases, e.g. leprosy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-immunity">Types of immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Innate immunity (body immunity)-genetic constitution or make up of an individual.</p>
<ul>
<li>1st line defence in combating pathogens.</li>
</ul>
<p>Divided into;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Non-specific-effective against wide range of infections by mechanical barriers or bactericidal substances (natural flora).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Specific or adaptive immunity-cellular immune system-cells</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>hummoral antibodies and compliment system</li>
</ul>
<p>B. Acquired immunity-antigen-anti body reaction or response.</p>
<p>Natural i) active- Larger popn acquiring a/bs via sickness.</p>
<p>ii) Passive-a/bs passed from mother to fetus in utero</p>
<p>Artificial i) -active-immunization with antigens</p>
<p>ii) Passive-immunization with a/bs</p>
<p>Herd immunity -80% immunization of target popn.</p>
<ul>
<li>Larger popn acquiring a/bs via sickness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-the-body-develops-immunity">How the body develops immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-the-body-develops-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>-two ways to acquire immunity against infections – active immunity and passive immunity.</p>
<ol>
<li>Active immunity is acquired when a person’s own immune system is stimulated to produce antigen specific antibodies and immune cells.</li>
</ol>
<p>This type of immunity often lasts for many years and it may be permanent.</p>
<p>Active immunity can be divided into</p>
<p>A) Natural active immunity-infections like measles disease.</p>
<p>B) Natural Passive Immunity</p>
<p>Passively acquired antibodies are responsible for the protection of newborns and young infants against certain diseases. The transfer of antibodies from mother to foetus across the placenta during the last 2-3 months of pregnancy provides the newborn with a portion of the mother’s immunological experience. Examples of passive transfer occur when:</p>
<p>produce antibodies, which when are in sufficient quantities, are able to identify the antigens and kill them or inactivate them. The patient recovers and the body's lymphocytes keep the memory of these organisms for life. This means that next time the same organism attacks the patient, the lymphocytes are ready to produce large amount of antibodies, which will overcome the organism. The patient will not get ill again hence he/she is said to have acquired natural immunity. For example, if a child has had measles and recovered, the child's lymphocytes produce antibodies any time the child encounters the measles virus through the body.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Artificial immunity-short lasting immunity as the body doesn't participate directly in production of antibodies.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-artificial-active-immunity">A) Artificial Active Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-artificial-active-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the type of immunity given through vaccine administration.</p>
<p>A vaccine is made from an organism which is either killed or attenuated, that means it has lost its harmfulness, or its part or toxin rendered harmless (“toxoid”).</p>
<ul>
<li>Also Artificial active immunity is acquired by-immunization by antigen eg LAV.</li>
</ul>
<p>However, its antigenicity will still be identified by lymphocytes and will induce production of antibodies.</p>
<p>For example if a child gets the oral polio vaccine (attenuated live polio virus), the child's body will produce antibodies against poliovirus and hence will be protected against poliomyelitis without having been sick.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-artificial-passive-immunity">B) Artificial Passive Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-artificial-passive-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>“Borrowed” antibodies can also protect one temporarily. These borrowed and prepared antibodies are from serum (antiserum) of person or animal that has been exposed to an antigen and has produced antibodies which are purified and are directly injected to the person at the site of infection to immediately counteract the offending antigen. Sources of passive artificial immunity include blood and blood products, immune or hyper-immune globulin, and animal antitoxins.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="comparison-of-the-different-types-of-immunity">Comparison of the different types of immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#comparison-of-the-different-types-of-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="active-immunity">Active Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#active-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Cause Infection, Immunisation with modified antigen</p>
<p>Advantage; Life long immunity Advantage Long lasting protection</p>
<p>Disadvantage; -Risk from dying from infection e.g. Measles</p>
<ul>
<li>No immediate protection (varies from 3-4weeks)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="passive-immunity">Passive Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#passive-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Transfer of Antibodies from mother’s blood to the fetus.</p>
<p>Also Borrowed antibodies from human or animal source (antiserum).</p>
<p>Advantage; Immediate protection, Immediate reaction</p>
<p>Disadvantage; Short lasting immunity, Adverse reaction may occur</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="herd-immunity">Herd Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#herd-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Immunity acquired when a higher proportion of immunized population in the community (children).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A community becomes susceptible to the disease if a large number of people who are not immune enter it either by birth or immigration (e.g. when an influx of unvaccinated refugees occurs in an area). There are two ways of developing herd immunity:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High natural infection rate in the community eg measles infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Artificial immunization. 80% immunized popns</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tetanus antibodies induced in the mother following immunization with tetanus toxoid easily passes across the placenta to the unborn child providing protection against tetanus in the neonatal period.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Measles antibodies made by the mother, passes through the placenta and breast milk, protecting the newborn during the first months of life.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Protection is better against some diseases (e.g. measles, rubella, tetanus) than others (e.g. polio, pertusis)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="natural-history-of-infection-or-disease">Natural History of Infection or disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-history-of-infection-or-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1st phase (entry and multiplication of infectious agent in the host) is marked by the progression from a healthy to a disease state. sub-clinical state.</p>
<p>2nd phase clinical phase - interaction between the pathogen / toxins and the body results in disease hence appearance of typical S/S. Is called incubation period. interval between exposure to an infectious agent and onset of clinical disease.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>3rd phase-recovery or convalescence phase-healing or full recovery or with disability stage or death.. depends on how well the body handles the pathogen or the toxin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-cause-of-infections">The cause of infections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-cause-of-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>are caused by organisms which get into the body through inhalation, ingestion, or Penetration of the skin/mucus membrane, vector borne, contact, congenital.</li>
<li>These organisms multiply in the body tissues/blood and cause illness.</li>
<li>Disease causing organisms include: bacteria, viruses, parasites and fungi.</li>
<li>Some microorganisms produce chemicals called toxins, which cause illnesses.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-of-vaccination">History of vaccination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-vaccination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Over 200 years ago, Edward Jenner first demonstrated that vaccination offered protection against smallpox, by cutting an arm of a boy (James Phipps) and placing the materials from cowpox (mild disease) into the wound. Later, he injected the boy with fluid from smallpox and the boy did not contract the smallpox disease. This experiment led to the inoculation of persons with relatively harmless disease materials which could protect them from a more dangerous disease.</li>
<li>This was called vaccination ("vacca" is Latin for cow). Since then the use of vaccines has continued to reduce the burden of many bacterial and viral diseases.</li>
<li>Small pox has been eradicated, and poliomyelitis no longer occurs in many regions of the world as a result of widespread effective vaccination.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="milestones-in-vaccine-development">Milestones in Vaccine Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#milestones-in-vaccine-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>1885: First use of live attenuated viral vaccine (rabies) in humans
1909: 1st live attenuated bacterial vaccine-Bacillus Calmette-Guerin(BCG) created for use against TB
1921: Diphtheria toxoid developed
1924: Tetanus toxoid produced
1930s: Pertussis vaccine developed
1932: Yellow fever vaccine developed
1940s: Diphtheria-tetanus-pertussis (DTP) combination introduced
1955: Inactivated polio vaccine introduced
1963: Live attenuated oral polio vaccine introduced
1963: Measles vaccine introduced
1986: First recombinant vaccine (hepatitis B) introduced
1990: First polysaccharide conjugate vaccine (Haemophilus influenzae type b) introduced</p>
<p>This was followed by faster introduction of Meningococcal conjugate (MCV4), Pneumococcal Conjugate vaccine, Rotavirus Vaccine and Human papillomavirus (HPV) whereas Malaria and HIV Vaccines are under development.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaccination-services-in-kenya">VACCINATION SERVICES IN KENYA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccination-services-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Vaccination against meningitis which is required by travelers proceeding for Umrah and Haj in Medina and Mecca in Saudi Arabia is obtained from private sector practitioners and through the Port Health Services.</li>
<li>The MOH established The Kenya Expanded Programme on Immunization (KEPI) in 1980 aimed at providing immunization against six killer diseases of childhood, namely tuberculosis, polio, diphtheria, whooping cough, tetanus and measles to all children in the country before their 1st birthday, and tetanus toxoid vaccination to all pregnant women. KEPI was part of the global Expanded Programmes on Immunization (EPIs), whose main goal was to control killer vaccine- preventable diseases of childhood.</li>
<li>Prior to 1980 vaccination services had been provided on an ad-hoc basis mainly through primary schools and the larger health institutions and facilities.</li>
<li>During the late 1970s the National Public Health Laboratories of the Ministry of Health used to manufacture smallpox and cholera vaccines and investigated all outbreaks of public health importance in Kenya.</li>
<li>Because of its role in the surveillance for and response to diseases of public health importance the N.P.H.Ls became the repository of all emergency vaccines eg Cholera, Hepatitis B, Typhoid, Rabies and Anti-snake venom.</li>
<li>However with the global eradication of smallpox, the N.P.H.Ls ceased manufacturing the small pox vaccine but continued to coordinate the use of the other emergency vaccines except for cholera which was phased out in the 1980s due to poor efficacy.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>From the early 1970s when international travel regulations mandated that travelers moving across countries must be appropriately vaccinated to prevent global transmission of regional endemic diseases, the Nairobi City Council Coordinated the vaccination of prospective overseas travelers with cholera and yellow fever vaccines.</li>
<li>Subsequently this role was taken up by the Department of Environmental Health within the MOH &amp; was administered through the Port Health Services in collaboration with the Department of Immigration.</li>
<li>The KEPI programme concentrated initially on establishing and strengthening the health service delivery.</li>
<li>However, in the 1990s, having achieved The Universal Child Immunization goals of immunizing at least 80% of the target population, KEPI’s focus changed to disease control, elimination and eradication.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-challenges-encountered-with-this-new-focus-included">The challenges encountered with this new focus included:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-challenges-encountered-with-this-new-focus-included" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Achieving and maintaining high routine immunization coverage in all sub counties.</li>
<li>Elimination of neonatal tetanus;</li>
<li>Eradication of poliomyelitis by the end of the year 2000;</li>
<li>Strengthening EPI disease surveillance.</li>
</ul>
<p>The co-ordination of procurement and distribution of special vaccines to respond to specific outbreak situations was under the Disease Outbreak Management Unit (D.O.M.U).</p>
<ul>
<li>This unit was under the MoH’s Division of Communicable Disease Control (D.C.D.C). DOMU’s role was to detect and respond to outbreaks of public health importance and institute an appropriate response.</li>
</ul>
<p>Where the outbreak is due to a vaccine preventable disease, DOMU sourced for the required specific vaccine and coordinated the response activities.</p>
<ul>
<li>DOMU did not maintain stocks of emergency vaccines, but advised on the specifications and quantities of vaccines required when necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p>The Division of Communicable Disease Control has since July 2007 been restructured and renamed the</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-of-vaccines-immunization-services-uvis-whereby-introduced-new-antigens-pcv10-rotavirus-ipv">Unit of Vaccines &amp; Immunization Services (UVIS) - whereby introduced new antigens-pcv10, rotavirus&amp;IPV.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-of-vaccines-immunization-services-uvis-whereby-introduced-new-antigens-pcv10-rotavirus-ipv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The UVIS exists to achieve the following objectives;</p>
<ul>
<li>To ensure equitable access to appropriate vaccination services for all persons in Kenya</li>
<li>To ensure universal immunization of children in Kenya with appropriate doses of MoH prescribed childhood vaccines.</li>
<li>To ensure universal immunization of special risk groups with MoH approved priority vaccines</li>
<li>To ensure optimum vaccination service delivery in response to specific situations of outbreak of life threatening vaccine or immunization preventable diseases; TB, polio, diphtheria, pertussis, Tetanus, measles, diarrhea, pneumonia, meningitis, yellow fever.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-objectives-of-the-unit-of-vaccines-immunization-services">The Objectives of the Unit of Vaccines &amp; Immunization Services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-objectives-of-the-unit-of-vaccines-immunization-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To ensure equitable access to appropriate vaccination services for all persons in Kenya</li>
<li>To ensure universal immunization of Kenyan children with appropriate doses of MOH prescribed childhood vaccines.</li>
<li>To ensure universal immunization of special risk groups with MOH approved priority vaccines</li>
<li>To ensure optimum vaccination service delivery in response to specific situations of outbreak of life threatening vaccine- preventable diseases eg Cholera, Hepatitis B, Typhoid, Rabies and Anti-snake venom.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="priority-activities-for-immunization-programme-are-as-follows">Priority activities for immunization programme are as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#priority-activities-for-immunization-programme-are-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Polio eradication through active surveillance.</li>
<li>Accelerated disease control</li>
<li>Improving performance of routine Immunization</li>
<li>Supplemental Immunization-campaigns</li>
<li>Improving financial flows from donor to service delivery points.</li>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-the-division-of-vaccines-immunization">ROLE OF THE DIVISION OF VACCINES &amp; IMMUNIZATION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-the-division-of-vaccines-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-policy-regulation-and-oversight">1 Policy Regulation and Oversight<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-policy-regulation-and-oversight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>i. Coordinating periodic reviews of the National Immunization Policy
ii. Developing and updating training guidelines and materials for immunization service delivery
iii. Facilitating the training of national and regional trainers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-commodity-security-and-quality-assurance">2. Commodity Security and Quality Assurance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-commodity-security-and-quality-assurance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i. To ensure continuous availability of adequate stocks of all MOH procured vaccines, related immunologicals and support logistics at all levels of service delivery.
ii. To monitor consumption of government supplied vaccines, antisera and vaccination devices used for human health within the Ministry.
iii. To monitor national immunization coverage trends and provide periodic reports.
iv. To monitor respective disease burden trends and correlate with immunization coverages (excluding comprehensive disease surveillance activities).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-monitoring-and-evaluation-m-e">3. Monitoring and evaluation(M&amp;E)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-monitoring-and-evaluation-m-e" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Develop multi-year and annual operational plans
ii. To set multi-year and annual performance targets</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-advocacy-and-resource-mobilization">4. Advocacy and Resource Mobilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-advocacy-and-resource-mobilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Annually review country wide vaccination social mobilization/advocacy needs.
ii. Develop and periodically revise social mobilization guidelines and strategies in line with vaccination performance trends in the country
iii. Determine multiyear and annual funding needs for universal immunization activities and develop comprehensive resource mobilization plans.
iv. Develop and periodically review resource mobilization guidelines and strategies in line with immunization funding needs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-capacity-strengthening">5. Capacity strengthening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-capacity-strengthening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Develop and periodically review guidelines and training materials/teaching aids on vaccine preventable diseases
ii. Spearhead the revision of curricula of medical institutions in relation to</p>
<ul>
<li>Current information on vaccine preventable diseases</li>
<li>Updates required by different cadres of health workers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-operational-research">6. Operational research<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-operational-research" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. To identify key operational research problems
ii. To identify resources and researchers to conduct the operational research</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-stakeholders-in-immunisation-service-provision">OTHER STAKEHOLDERS IN IMMUNISATION SERVICE PROVISION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-stakeholders-in-immunisation-service-provision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>DDSR - Division of Disease Surveillance and Response</li>
<li>KEMRI - Kenya Medical Research Institute - Lab investigations in cases of suspected epidermic</li>
<li>NPHLs - National Public Health Laboratories investigations in cases of suspected epidermic</li>
<li>Private sector players in health eg Nairobi, Agakhan, MP shah etc Hospitals</li>
<li>Training institutions e.g. Universities, mid level training institutions - KMTC</li>
<li>PPB – Pharmacy and Poisons Board</li>
<li>NITAG – National Immunization Technical Advisory Group</li>
<li>Philanthropic individuals and associations like Agakhan foundation, Elizabeth Glaciers etc</li>
<li>Civil society organisations eg Amani Kenya</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-system-components">Immunization System Components<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-system-components" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-immunization-service-delivery">1. Immunization Service Delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-immunization-service-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>UVIS programme endeavors to sustain and improve on the gains made over the years by providing Quality immunization services (potent antigens).</li>
<li>In Kenya, primarily most of immunizations take place in fixed posts ie H/facilities plus</li>
<li>Others; outreach clinic, mobile clinics and Supplemental Immunization Activities (campaigns) play a role in improving service delivery especially hard to reach popns.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-vaccine-supply-quality-and-logistics">1. Vaccine Supply, Quality and Logistics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-vaccine-supply-quality-and-logistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>UVIS ensures that adequate vaccines as well as injection materials are procured through WHO/UNICEF approved mechanisms (infant vaccines) as well as through the GoK. (KEPI/non-EPI vaccines). procurement system from manufacturer in Netherlands. Received at Airport to the national storage centre, distributed to respective regional centres the Subcounty H/offices order and collect. H/facilities order using S11.</li>
<li>Vaccines are received using Stock Control ledge books and stored in KEPI fridge.</li>
<li>Transported out and into fridge using vaccine carriers with sponge and frozen icepacks to maintain potency.</li>
<li>UVIS internal quality assurance mechanisms ascertain vaccine quality is maintained up to the point of utilization (SDP).</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Logistics should be put in place before starting immunization session eg working equipment, accessories etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-disease-surveillance">3. Disease Surveillance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-disease-surveillance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The Disease Surveillance and Response Unit (DSRU) is responsible for disease surveillance and response activities working in liaison with county and Sub County Disease Surveillance Coordinators.</li>
<li>UVIS will liaise closely with DSRU for all vaccine preventable diseases.</li>
<li>Vaccine preventable disease surveillance data (Polio, measles, neonatal tetanus) is monitored so as to address gaps in immunization coverage in a timely manner as appropriate.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-advocacy-social-mobilization-and-communication">4. Advocacy, social Mobilization and Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-advocacy-social-mobilization-and-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Advocacy, social mobilization and communication are very crucial in EPI services.</li>
<li>The advocacy unit at UVIS aims to assist in effective implementation of the planned activities as well as increase demand for service by communities.</li>
<li>To this end, the unit develops and disseminates EPI communication plan for both routine immunization as well as SIAs.</li>
<li>In addition, the unit develops key EPI messages for both the health workers and the community, which are disseminated through various channels and strategies ie IEC materials in MCH/FP clinics.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-supportive-components">5. Supportive components;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-supportive-components" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-management">a) Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The management functions deals with people, resources and information.</li>
</ul>
<p>The roles of managers include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Policy making</li>
<li>Setting standards</li>
<li>Proper utilization of resources located towards immunization activities.</li>
<li>Developing IEC materials distributed to the SDPs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-sustainable-financing">b) Sustainable financing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-sustainable-financing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Vaccination services are expensive and often not adequately funded. For EPI programme to realize its goals and objectives there is need for sustainable financing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>UVIS therefore has to have capacity to do the following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Budgeting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Identifying funding sources</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Actions to increase resources allocation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These activities are meant to ensure that the programme activities are not disrupted due to lack of finances, especially for commodities as well as fuel that runs the cold-chain.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-human-and-institutional-resources">c) Human and institutional resources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-human-and-institutional-resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Like any medical field, immunization practices are constantly changing.</p>
<p>The EPI programme must have the capacity to do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Staffing</li>
<li>Training</li>
<li>Supervision</li>
<li>Institutional support</li>
<li>Technical information</li>
<li>Support to research projects</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-vaccines-used-in-by-the-kenya-uvis">Types of Vaccines used in by the Kenya UVIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-vaccines-used-in-by-the-kenya-uvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are three types of vaccine:</p>
<ul>
<li>Live attenuated vaccines</li>
<li>KILLED or Inactivated vaccines – either whole cell or cell fractions</li>
<li>Genetically engineered (recombinant) vaccines – which are similar to inactivated vaccines</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-live-attenuated-vaccines">1. Live attenuated vaccines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-live-attenuated-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Derived from disease-causing viruses or bacteria that have been weakened under laboratory conditions.</li>
<li>They will multiply in a vaccinated individual by causing disease in a mild form.</li>
<li>Only one dose of this type of vaccine provides life-long immunity, except OPV, which requires multiple doses.</li>
<li>LAVs divided into 2 types;</li>
<li>Virus: oral polio vaccine (OPV), measles, yellow fever</li>
<li>Bacteria: BCG, oral typhoid (Salmonella typhi) and oral cholera</li>
</ul>
<p>NB-BCG, OPV, Measles &amp; Yellow fever are EPI LAVs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-inactivated-or-killed-vaccines">2. Inactivated or killed vaccines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-inactivated-or-killed-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Produced by growing viruses or bacteria then inactivating them with heat or chemicals.</li>
<li>Cannot grow in a vaccinated individual (killed) and therefore cannot cause the disease.</li>
<li>Multiple doses are required for full protection (killed non-effective).</li>
<li>Booster doses are needed to maintain immunity because protection by these vaccines diminishes over time.</li>
<li>Divided into 2 types;</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Whole-cell vaccines are made of an entire bacterial or viral cell taken from their surface capsules.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Whole inactivated viral vaccines, e.g. Smallpox, Injectable Polio Vaccine (IPV) (Salk), hepatitis A, Influenza, antirabies.</li>
<li>Whole inactivated bacterial vaccines, e.g. whole-cell pertussis, inactivated cholera, anthrax</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Subunit and fractional vaccine - These vaccines are composed of parts (i.e. subunits or fractions) of the pathogen, instead of the whole pathogen, e.g. Fractional: Diphtheria and tetanus toxoids, Haemophilus influenzae type b conjugate vaccine (Hib), pneumococcal conjugate vaccine (PCV)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-recombinant-or-conjugate-vaccines">3. Recombinant or conjugate vaccines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-recombinant-or-conjugate-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Vaccines are produced by inserting genetic material from a disease-causing organism into a harmless cell, which replicates the proteins of the disease-causing organism.</li>
<li>The proteins are then purified and used as vaccine</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples: pentavalent; Hepatitis B, HIB, TT, Diphtheria, pertussis</p>
<p>Sub types Recombinant or conjugate vaccines</p>
<p>Monovalent vaccine - single antigen protecting against one disease or MOs</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Bivalent vaccine-antigen against two strains of disease causing mos.eg Bopv-type 1&amp;3strains of polio viruses,two strains of HPV.</p>
<p>Trivalent vaccine-antigen against 3 strains of disease causing otgs eg OPv,influenza A,B&amp;C</p>
<p>Polyvalent-antigen against two or strains of disease causing organisms eg penta,MMR, 10 valent pneumococcal conjugate vaccine(PCV10)</p>
<p>Liquid vaccines-OPV,IPV,ROTA,Penta,</p>
<p>Lymphosized vaccines-</p>
<p>SUMMARY OF CHILDHOOD IMMUNIZABLE DISEASES</p>
<p>EPI vaccines currently in use:</p>
<ul>
<li>BCG</li>
<li>Oral Polio/inactivated polio vaccine (IPV)</li>
<li>DPT/HepB-Hib (Pentavalent)</li>
<li>PCV10</li>
<li>Measles</li>
<li>Tetanus Toxoid</li>
<li>Rota virus</li>
<li>Yellow Fever</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kepi-vaccines-and-technique-of-administration">KEPI VACCINES AND TECHNIQUE OF ADMINISTRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kepi-vaccines-and-technique-of-administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bcg-bacilli-calmette-guerin-vaccine">BCG - Bacilli Calmette-Guerin vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bcg-bacilli-calmette-guerin-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>BCG is a freeze-dried (powder) live attenuated vaccine prepared from <em>Mycobacterium Bovis</em>.</p>
<p>It has a lifespan of up to 12 months from the date of preparation, when kept under the right temperature of +2°C to +8°C. Reconstituted with cold diluent provided to make 20 dose vial.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-why-do-you-give-bcg">a) Why do you give BCG?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-why-do-you-give-bcg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Protects against tuberculosis (TB) common diseases in Kenya. Also against leprosy.</li>
<li>BCG prevents severe forms of TB, e.g. TB meningitis and TB in non-immunised infants.</li>
<li>This is why it is so important to begin immunization at birth as recommended by the National Immunization Schedule.</li>
<li>BCG immunity is estimated to last between 7-15 years.</li>
<li>Only one administration is recommended in the schedule.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-how-to-store-the-bcg-vaccine-at-facility-level">b) How to store the BCG vaccine at facility level.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-how-to-store-the-bcg-vaccine-at-facility-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>BCG vaccine should be stored continuously at +2°C to +8°C.</li>
<li>Monitor Vaccine Vial Monitor (VVM).</li>
<li>Stored at the coolest part of the refrigerator.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-when-should-you-give-bcg">c) When should you give BCG?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-when-should-you-give-bcg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>BCG vaccine should be given at birth or at first contact.</li>
<li>BCG vaccine is usually given to children up to the age of 5 years, if no BCG scar is present.</li>
<li>Contacts of persons above 15 years who are not suffering from TB and have a negative mantoux test, should be immunized with BCG immediately.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="d-when-not-to-give-bcg">d) When not to give BCG:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-when-not-to-give-bcg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>If symptomatic HIV/AIDS and other known immune-suppression diseases e.g. cancers.</li>
<li>BCG should also be withheld in cases of acute illness (fever) needing hospitalization but be given on discharge.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="e-how-to-give-bcg-route-site-and-dose">e) How to give BCG, Route, site and dose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-how-to-give-bcg-route-site-and-dose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Given through intradermally on left arm, most efficient in immune conversion.</li>
<li>It produces a lasting scar as an indicator for immunization</li>
<li>The dose is 0.05 ml for children less than 1 year or 0.1 ml for children above 1 year.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="f-what-are-the-requirements-for-administering-bcg-vaccine">f) What are the requirements for administering BCG vaccine?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-what-are-the-requirements-for-administering-bcg-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Sterile AD BCG syringes with needles gauge 26.</li>
<li>Sterile 2ml reconstituting syringe and needles gauge 21</li>
<li>Safety box</li>
<li>A vaccine carrier with ice packs and a sponge</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Refuse bin</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>g) How to prepare the BCG vaccine:</strong></p>
<p>Always open vial of BCG vaccine with great care, because sometimes a vacuum is maintained inside the ampoule.</p>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands</li>
<li>Dilute the vaccine under sterile conditions with a cold diluent.</li>
<li>Transfer the diluent with a dry sterile 2 ml syringe using gauge 21 long needle into the ampoule/vial containing the vaccine.</li>
<li>Gently mix the vaccine well before filling the syringe.</li>
<li>Withdraw the vaccine with needle and syringe, and then discharge it back into the ampoule twice or thrice to give a homogenous solution.</li>
<li>If the vaccine comes in a vial, use non-touch technique and withdraw the diluent and mix as described above.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> in case of ampoule</p>
<ul>
<li>File the ampoule on the neck.</li>
<li>Take care to avoid harming yourself by covering the ampoule neck with clean cotton swab</li>
<li>Break the ampoule neck.</li>
<li><strong>Remember, BCG is very sensitive to sunlight and heat.</strong></li>
<li>Keep the reconstituted vaccine in a sponge with a slit in a vaccine carrier.</li>
<li><strong>BCG potency lasts for six hours after being reconstituted.</strong></li>
<li>Reconstitute the vaccine as soon as the first eligible child for BCG reports at the clinic.</li>
<li>Record time of reconstitution.</li>
<li>Discard reconstituted BCG vaccine after 6 hours or at the end of immunization session whichever comes first.</li>
<li>Never store diluted BCG vaccine for next day’s use.</li>
<li>Open a BCG vaccine vial even if only one child is to be given the immunization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>i) How to fill the syringe:</strong></p>
<p>Allow the ampoule/vial to stand upright on the sponge in the vaccine carrier for about one minute to let bubbles disappear. Fill the syringe with the required dose of the vaccine using the BCG AD syringe.</p>
<p>Withdraw one dose at a time to avoid exposure of the reconstituted BCG vaccine.</p>
<p>Measure the volume of vaccine to be injected according to the markings on the barrel of the 0.05 ml syringe for children less than 1 year and 0.1 ml syringe for children over 1 year.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Do not withdraw several doses in advance.</p>
<p><strong>j) How to inject the vaccine:</strong></p>
<p>With your left hand, hold the left forearm of the child to be immunized.</p>
<ul>
<li>Stretch the skin over the site between your left index finger and thumb.</li>
<li>Introduce the needle upwards, into the skin, keeping it as flat as possible, so as to give it intradermally.</li>
<li>Inject BCG vaccine intradermally on the outer (dorsal) aspect of the left forearm at the junction of the upper and middle thirds.</li>
<li>When you give the injection intradermally into the lower layer of the skin, a weal appears (about 7-8 mm) with small pits on it like an orange peel.</li>
<li>Remove the needle and do not rub the site.</li>
<li>Caution the parent/guardian not to rub the site or apply anything on it.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>k) What happens after BCG IMMUNIZATION?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The wheal (about 7-8 mm) will form and disappear in about half an hour.</li>
<li>After two weeks a small red induration nodule (measuring about 10 mm) appears and lasts for about two weeks or more.</li>
<li>Sometimes the nodule may appear earlier (in <strong>s</strong>d <strong>studocu</strong> means that the individual had a</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>certain degree of hypersensitivity. This is called an "accelerated indurated reaction".</p>
<p>When they do, reassure the parent/guardian and refer child for further management.</p>
<ul>
<li>Excessive ulceration is when an ulcer is still present more than 12 weeks after immunization, or one which is more than 1 cm. No treatment is required but apply a sterile dry dressing.</li>
<li>Lymph node enlargements sometimes occur. If they ulcerate refer for further management.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="m-bcg-records">m) BCG records:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#m-bcg-records" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Remember to record the immunization in.</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklet</li>
<li>Tally Sheet-transfer to monthly immunization summary for reporting.</li>
<li>Permanent Child Register</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> BCG is the first vaccine you give to every child.</p>
<p>Therefore, this being the first contact with the child and mother, a positive first impression will encourage her to seek further immunization.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="polio-vaccine">POLIO VACCINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#polio-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Oral Polio Vaccine (OPV) is a live attenuated vaccine made from the three types of polio virus: type I, II and III.</p>
<p>It is ready for use in a vial. The vaccine is very sensitive to heat and light.</p>
<p>Injectable Polio Vaccine (IPV) is given by intramuscular injection at 10wks</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-why-do-you-give-oral-polio-vaccine">a) Why do you give oral polio vaccine?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-why-do-you-give-oral-polio-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>It is given at birth since there is no maternal antibodies transfer.</li>
<li>It induces intestinal immunity, besides producing antibodies in blood.</li>
<li>OPV coverage of 80% and above induces herd immunity.</li>
<li>It is simple to administer orally, well accepted by children and mothers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-when-do-you-give-opv">b) When do you give OPV?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-when-do-you-give-opv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>At birth or at first contact with the child up to 2 weeks to avoid interfering with schedule.</p>
<ul>
<li>First OPV should be given at six weeks or at first contact with child after that age, together with first DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine.</li>
<li>Second OPV should be given at 10 weeks or at next contact with child after that age, together with second DPT/HepB+Hib.</li>
<li>Third OPV should be given at 14 weeks or at the next contact with child together with third DPT/HepB+Hib.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The birth dose is counted as a Zero dose since the uptake of vaccine to the infants has not developed adequately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="storage">Storage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Store OPV at +2°C to +8°C at facility level.</li>
<li>Monitor Vaccine Vial Monitor (VVM).</li>
<li>Stored at the coolest part of the refrigerator.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The interval between the first, second and third doses must be at least one month apart. If you give the next dose of OPV before this minimum period of one month, there will be an interruption in the formation of antibodies.</p>
<p>There is no maximum time interval between two doses.</p>
<p>Even if a year passes between successive doses of vaccine, do not begin the series again, as was the practice in the past.</p>
<p>But remember, these delays the time when the child is protected.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-when-should-you-not-give-opv">c) When should you not give OPV?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-when-should-you-not-give-opv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Besides known impaired immunity, diarrhoea&amp;vomiting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="d-how-to-give-opv">d) How to give OPV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-how-to-give-opv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands.</li>
<li>Always arrange to give the vaccine indoors or in the shade because it is very sensitive to heat and light.</li>
<li>Keep OPV in a vaccine carrier throughout the immunization session between +2 to +8°C.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Use the dropper or device supplied with vaccine.</li>
<li>Put two drops, or as prescribed by the manufacturers, into the child’s mouth.</li>
<li>If the child does not open the mouth, gently squeeze the child’s nose between two fingers.</li>
<li>Do not touch the child’s lips or tongue with the dropper. If this happens, finish giving the vaccine to the child, then discards the dropper.</li>
<li>Make sure the child swallows. If the child spits the vaccine out, repeat the dosage.</li>
<li>Make sure the mother knows the date for the next dose.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>f) What are the possible reactions/complications?</strong></p>
<p>Vaccine reactions associated to paralytic polio are very rare.</p>
<p><strong>e) OPV recording</strong></p>
<p>Remember to record the immunization given in the;</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklet.</li>
<li>Immunization tally sheet- transfer to monthly immunization summary for reporting.</li>
<li>Immunization permanent register.</li>
</ul>
