<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pentavalent-dpt-hepb-hib-vaccine">PENTAVALENT-DPT/HepB+Hib Vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pentavalent-dpt-hepb-hib-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>a) Why do you give DPT/HepB+Hib?</strong></p>
<p>It protects against five diseases namely; diphtheria, pertusis, tetanus, hepatitis B, and Haemophilus influenza type B (Pneumonia, meningitis and epiglottitis).</p>
<p><strong>b) When should you give DPT/HepB+Hib?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Give the first dose of DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine at the age of six weeks or at first contact with the child anytime after that age, together with first OPV and BCG if not given before.</li>
<li>If you give DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine before six weeks, the child may not be protected and can get the disease you are trying to protect them from.</li>
<li>The minimum interval is one month as is with OPV. There is no maximum interval but, the sooner the child completes the series the sooner the child is protected.</li>
<li>Second DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine should be given at 10 weeks of age, or at the next contact with the child after that age, together with 2nd OPV.</li>
<li>Third DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine should be given at the age of 14 weeks, or at the next contact with child after that age, together with third OPV</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NB-Currently no booster dose is given.</strong></p>
<p><strong>c) When not to give DPT/HepB+Hib:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A child reported with convulsions after the previous dose. The “P”-pertusis component is Likely to cause convulsions, in such cases withhold the vaccine and refer the child to the clinician.</li>
<li>Unexplained Fever of unknown cause.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>d) What are the requirements for administration of DPT/HepB+Hib?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>AD syringe and needle</li>
<li>Vaccine carrier with sponge.</li>
<li>DPT/HepB+Hib Vaccine</li>
<li>Reconditioned ice-packs</li>
<li>Waste disposal bin</li>
<li>Dry single use cotton wool in a galipot.</li>
<li>File top remover</li>
<li>Safety boxes.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> During the immunization session, keep DPT/HepB+Hib on a sponge in a vaccine carrier with conditioned ice packs.</p>
<p><strong>e) How to give it:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The dose is 0.5 ml. Given intramuscularly in the Lt upper outer aspect of the thigh.</li>
<li>Do not inject in the buttocks because of the danger of injuring the sciatic nerve causing paralysis.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>f) How to prepare to give the vaccine</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands under running water</li>
</ul>
<p>Studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Clean/swab the site if visibly dirty with freshly prepared swab,</li>
<li>Divide the thigh into four imaginary quarters and take the upper outer part of the thigh as the injection site. The intra-muscular route induces efficient conversion and produces minimal reactions.</li>
<li>Place your thumb and index finger on each side of the place where you intend to inject and stretch the skin slightly.</li>
<li>Carefully push the needle into the space between your fingers.
Go deep into the muscle so as to give an intra-muscular injection.</li>
<li>Withdraw the needle and immediately discard it into the safety box.</li>
<li>If site is bleeding apply slight pressure with a dry swab.</li>
<li>Discard used swabs into a waste disposal bin.</li>
<li>Tell the mother when to bring the child back for the next immunization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pneumoccocal-vaccine">PNEUMOCCOCAL VACCINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pneumoccocal-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dosage-and-route-of-administration-for-pcv10">Dosage and route of administration for PCV10:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage-and-route-of-administration-for-pcv10" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>0.5mls of vaccine injected intramuscularly into the anterior upper, outer aspects of the right thigh in three doses given at 6, 10 and 14 weeks of age.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="same-as-penta">Same as penta.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#same-as-penta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Protects against bacterium <em>Streptococcus pneumoniae</em> (pneumococcus), which has more than 91 known serotypes, such as pneumonia (community acquired pneumonia), meningitis and bacteremia. OTHERS such as sinusitis and otitis media.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rotavirus-vaccine">ROTAVIRUS VACCINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rotavirus-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rotaviruses are a genus of viruses belonging to the Reoviridae family. Seven major groups have been identified, three of which (groups A, B, and C) infect humans, with group A being the most common and widespread one.</p>
<p>Protects against severe forms diarrhea in children caused by Rotavirus</p>
<p>The four commonest rota virus strains in Kenya are:</p>
<ul>
<li>G8P[6]</li>
<li>G10P(8)</li>
<li>G1P (6)</li>
<li>G9P(8)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="vaccine-type">Vaccine type:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-type" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Two types of live attenuated virus formulations for oral administration are licensed locally.</p>
<ul>
<li>A monovalent formulation (Rotarix™) which protects against serotypes G1P8 and possibly non G1 serotypes such as G2, G3, G4 and G9</li>
<li>A pentavalent formulation (RotaTeq™) which protects against serotypes <em>G serotypes</em> - human G1, G2, G3 and G4; bovine G6; human P1A[8] and bovine P7[5]</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dosage">Dosage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Vaccination course for the monovalent vaccine consists of two doses.
The first dose should be given between 6 and 14 weeks and the second between 14-24 weeks of age.
The interval between doses should not be less than 4 weeks.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="measles-vaccine-mmr">Measles Vaccine-MMR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measles-vaccine-mmr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a freeze dried (powder) live attenuated vaccine that has to be reconstituted with a cold</p>
<p>Diluent that is provided with the vaccine. It is supplied in 10 dose vial.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-when-should-you-give-measles-vaccine">a) When should you give measles vaccine?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-when-should-you-give-measles-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Maternal antibodies seem to remain in most children until the age of 6 to 9 months.</li>
<li>If children are immunized before the age of 9 months, most of them might not be protected.</li>
<li>This might lead to same mothers losing faith in the immunization.</li>
<li>Immunization against measles with the present vaccine should not start earlier than 9 months.</li>
<li>Measles vaccine can be given at the same time with any other vaccine e.g. a late penta, opv, BCG, pcv10</li>
<li>Give measles vaccine at 9 months or at first contact with the child after that age 18mons as second dose (booster)</li>
<li>Measles vaccine should be administered to all children admitted to the ward if they have not been immunized with two documented doses before and have no history of measles infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>b) When not to give measles vaccine:
Measles vaccine should not be given to critically ill hospitalized children, but make sure it is given on discharge.</p>
<p>c) What are the requirements for administration of Measles?</p>
<ul>
<li>AD syringe and needle</li>
<li>A sterile 2mls reconstituting syringe and needle gauge 21</li>
<li>Vaccine carrier with sponge.</li>
<li>DPT/HepB+Hib Vaccine</li>
<li>Reconditioned ice-packs</li>
<li>Waste disposal bin</li>
<li>Dry single use cotton wool in a galipot.</li>
<li>File top remover</li>
<li>Safety boxes.</li>
</ul>
<p>d) How to prepare to give measles vaccine (Refer to manufacturers guidelines)</p>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands.</li>
<li>Remove the top cover of the diluent and of the measles vaccine to expose the rubber cap. Clean both tops with a cotton swab soaked in water. Note: The Measles diluent must be at the same temperature as the vaccine.</li>
<li>Prepare the syringe to withdraw the diluent.</li>
<li>Introduce the needle to the rubber top of the diluent and withdraw the amount required as recommended by the manufacturer.</li>
<li>Discard the empty diluent bottle.</li>
<li>Without contaminating the needle, introduce the diluent to the measles vaccine bottle. Shake the bottle a little to mix thoroughly before withdrawing vaccine.</li>
<li>Withdraw 0.5 ml, the remaining measles vaccine and keep it in a sponge in a vaccine carrier.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note: Be careful not to expose the Measles vaccine to heat, light or contact with antiseptic or disinfectants as they destroy the vaccine</p>
<p>f) How to inject the vaccine:
The dose is 0.5 ml. Give measles vaccine subcutaneous in the outer side of the right upper arm, in the deltoid muscle as illustrated below at 45 degrees. (Confirm with the manufactures</p>
<ul>
<li>Show the mother how to hold the child firmly.</li>
<li>This is a subcutaneous injection. Inject the same way as the DPT/HepB+Hib vaccine.</li>
<li>Tell the mother about the possible reactions after measles vaccine, e.g. slight fever, running nose occurring 5 to 10 days after immunization, slight rash.</li>
</ul>
<p>This mild illness shows that the vaccine is working to protect the child. The illness is always much less serious than the disease.</p>
<p>Note: Remember to record the immunization given:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklet.</li>
<li>Immunization tally sheet- transfer to monthly immunization summary for reporting.</li>
<li>Immunization permanent register.</li>
<li>Discard measles vaccine 6 hours after reconstitution.(non-potent)hi</li>
<li>Always remember to reassure the mother.</li>
</ul>
<p>g) What can go wrong? Non-conversion of immunized children:</p>
<ul>
<li>The child may not have measles but some other viral infection with a similar rash and fever.</li>
<li>Measles vaccine lost it's potency due to improper storage that was used.</li>
<li>The child immunized may have been too young (before 9 months) and still had many antibodies from the mother.</li>
<li>use of expired vaccine administered to the child.</li>
<li>Child had already acquired antibodies from an illness.</li>
<li>The measles vaccine failure rate is 15% and the child may simply be among these.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is expected that if proper methods and vaccines are used for immunization, the immunity derived</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>is lifelong.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="h-follow-up">h) Follow-up<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#h-follow-up" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Measles is the last vaccine to be given to the child. This does not mean the child doesn't need to come to the MCH clinic any more. The mother should keep on bringing him/her on a regular basis, as often as she can (once a month or at least quarterly), for weighing, growth monitoring Vit A Supplementation and any advice, especially on nutrition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-national-immunization-schedule">The national immunization schedule<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-national-immunization-schedule" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fully immunized child - received all scheduled antigens before celebrating 1st birth day.</p>
<p>There is an optimal age for each vaccine: BCG and OPV0 are given at birth. DPT+HepB-Hib and pneumococcal vaccines should be commenced at age 6 weeks. If given earlier, they will not provide protection.</p>
<p>Measles vaccine should not be given before nine months due to presence of significant blood levels of maternal antibodies that lower its efficacy.</p>
<p>All series antigens, the three doses of OPV, DPT+HepB-Hib and PCV should be given one month apart to let the child's immune system process the previous dose and produce the best antibody response.</p>
<p>If the mother comes later than four weeks after the previous dose, the doses should be continued.</p>
<p>DO not restart the schedule since there is no maximum interval between doses and the vaccine will be as effective as if given after four weeks; however encourage the mother not to forget the next appointment.</p>
<p>NB: Do not miss an opportunity to immunize when you see an eligible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="yellow-fever-vaccine">Yellow Fever Vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#yellow-fever-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Is a live attenuated freeze-dried, vaccine that must be reconstituted with the Diluent provided.</p>
<p>The vaccine must be discarded six hours after reconstitution or at the end of the immunization session, whichever comes first.</p>
<p>b) When should you give it?</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>One dose should be given to children at nine months of age or at first contact, at the same time as measles vaccine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1992 in the Kerio Valley and mass vaccination was conducted in Baringo, Keiyo, Koibatek and Marakwet districts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No cases of yellow fever have since been reported from these districts and in Kenya.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>c) When not to give it:</p>
<p>WHO recommends vaccine should not be given to patients with symptomatic HIV/unexplained fever.</p>
<p>d) How to give it:</p>
<p>The 0.5 ml dose is given subcutaneously in the upper Right arm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tetanus-toxoid-vaccine-tt">Tetanus Toxoid Vaccine (TT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus-toxoid-vaccine-tt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a relatively heat stable vaccine prepared by formalin treatment of the toxin produced by Clostridium Tetani (mainly the Harvard strain).</p>
<p>The most commonly used type of toxoid is the adsorbed one because the antitoxin response reaches higher titres which last longer.</p>
<p>Note: The concentration of toxoid in the single dose adult preparations is similar to that in the paediatric preparations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-why-do-you-give-this-immunization">a) Why do you give this immunization?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-why-do-you-give-this-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>You give it to prevent tetanus disease, because there is no natural immunity to tetanus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TT is given regardless of age.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>-Pregnant women are immunized so that they provide maternal antibodies to unborn babies which protect them against neonatal tetanus-disease targeted for eradication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-when-not-to-give-it">b) When not to give it:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-when-not-to-give-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>No known contraindications for giving TT vaccine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-store-the-vaccine">How to store the vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-store-the-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus toxoid should be stored continuously at +2° C to +8° C</li>
<li>Tetanus toxoid should never be frozen as this reduces its potency.</li>
<li>Tetanus toxoid vaccine that has been exposed to freezing temperatures should never be used.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-administer-the-vaccine">How to administer the vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-administer-the-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>0.5 ml of the liquid is drawn into an AD syringe</li>
<li>Through IM injection into the left upper arm into the deltoid muscle or non-dominant hand.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="documentation-tools">Documentation tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#documentation-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The immunization tally sheet</li>
<li>The permanent TT Register</li>
<li>The Ante-natal Register</li>
<li>The TT injection register or booklet.</li>
<li>The immunization summary sheet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-reactions">Common Reactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-reactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The main local reactions are; pain, swelling, numbness and redness at the injection site but these are usually self-limiting and do not require treatment.</li>
<li>Should a person develop a severe reaction after being injected with tetanus toxoid, then the next dose must be differed until a qualified medical opinion is obtained.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="opportunities-for-giving-5-tetanus-toxoid-vaccination-schedule">OPPORTUNITIES FOR GIVING 5-TETANUS TOXOID VACCINATION SCHEDULE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opportunities-for-giving-5-tetanus-toxoid-vaccination-schedule" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The aim of the 5-TT schedule is to provide about 20 years + of protection against this killer disease for those at risk and especially for women of childbearing age and their unborn babies.</li>
<li>There are main opportunities for the administration of the 5-Tetanus Toxoid schedule.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-5-tt-for-focused-antenatal-care-fanc">1.5-TT FOR FOCUSED ANTENATAL CARE (FANC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-5-tt-for-focused-antenatal-care-fanc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is given as part of Focused Antenatal Care – FANC</li>
<li>Vaccination against tetanus is given during pregnancy episodes</li>
<li>Doses are documented and when a woman has received 5-doses (usually by the fourth pregnancy) no further doses should be given in subsequent pregnancies.</li>
<li>After receiving 5 well spaced doses of tetanus toxoid vaccine the woman would have developed immunity for approximately 20 years, and in most cases this is long enough to cover the rest of her reproductive life.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-t-t-schedule-for-pregnancy">5-T.T. SCHEDULE for PREGNANCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-t-t-schedule-for-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>First pregnancy 1st TT dose (given from the fourth to sixth month i.e. 2nd trimester)</p>
<p>2nd TT dose given one month after the 1st dose (between the fifth &amp; eighth month)</p>
<p>Works as an immunological primer but does not confer protection against maternal tetanus at delivery.</p>
<p>Confers protection from maternal tetanus at delivery &amp; for about 1 – 3 years from tetanus in general however approx. 10% may respond poorly to 2nd dose</p>
<p>No protection from tetanus at birth! Confers protection at birth (PAB) for ≥90% of neonates due to</p>
<p>adequate titres of maternal antibodies</p>
<p>Second pregnancy 3rd TT dose (given anytime between the forth &amp; eighth months) Immunity boosted for 5</p>
<p>years</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Third Pregnancy 4th TT dose (given anytime between the fourth &amp; eighth month) Immunity boosted for 10 years</p>
<p>Fourth pregnancy 5th TT &amp; last dose (given anytime between the fourth &amp; eighth month) Immunity boosted for 20 years</p>
<p>Subsequent pregnancies - No more TT doses Immunity adequate for rest of parous life</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-5-tt-for-girls-and-women-of-child-bearing-age-cbaws">5. 5-TT For GIRLS AND WOMEN OF CHILD BEARING AGE (CBAWS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-5-tt-for-girls-and-women-of-child-bearing-age-cbaws" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tetanus toxoid vaccination is given to females aged between 15 to 49 years irrespective of their pregnancy status or reproductive health goals</p>
<ul>
<li>The lower and upper age limits can be varied according to local experience of childbearing patterns.</li>
<li>The lower and upper age limits can be varied according to local experience of childbearing patterns.</li>
<li>This schedule builds up the immunity of the girl or woman for the assumed eventuality of pregnancy and childbirth for herself and her future babies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-5-tt-for-trauma-and-occupational-prophylaxis">6. 5-TT for Trauma and Occupational prophylaxis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-5-tt-for-trauma-and-occupational-prophylaxis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This schedule is usually initiated in the event of trauma and the tetanus toxoid doses should be given in the prescribed intervals until all 5 doses have been given.</li>
<li>After: After the five doses, recipients would have acquired immunity against tetanus for 20 years.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-5-tt-schedule-for-school-aged-children">7. 5-TT schedule for school-aged children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-tt-schedule-for-school-aged-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A special programme restricted to the districts of coast province</p>
<p>Remember to record the immunization in 3 places</p>
<ul>
<li>TT Card/Mother’s ANC Card</li>
<li>Permanent TT Register</li>
<li>Tally Sheet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="g-what-happens-after-immunization">g) What happens after immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#g-what-happens-after-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It may cause a little pain and swelling at the injection site for two or three days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-vaccines-in-terms-of-preparation">Types of vaccines in terms of preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-vaccines-in-terms-of-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Liquid-soln form - OPV, IPV, PCV10, TT, ROTA. Sensitive to freezing.</li>
<li>Lyophilized (freeze dried or powder) or reconstituted vaccines - BCG, Measles, Yellow fever. Sensitive to heat or sunlight.</li>
</ol>
<p>ASSIGNMENT; Components of vaccine; Antigen, diluent, adjuvants, stabilizers, preservatives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-qualities-of-an-ideal-vaccine">Characteristics/qualities of an ideal vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-qualities-of-an-ideal-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Safety - free from any harm</li>
<li>Cost effective - affordable to the government &amp; local mwananchi.</li>
<li>Thermal stability - able to tolerate heat to maintain potency.</li>
<li>Efficacy - ability to induce or confer long term immunity.</li>
<li>Easy to administer - eg orally</li>
<li>Multivalency - able to prevent many or multiple diseases.</li>
<li>Herd immunity - able to confer protection to a large proportion of popn ie 80-90%.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-reminders-guidelines-principles">IMMUNIZATION REMINDERS/Guidelines/principles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-reminders-guidelines-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use every opportunity to Keep vaccines cold at +2 to +8 degrees centigrade at all the time especially during immunization sessions, particularly OPV, BCG and measles.</li>
<li>Record batch numbers in stock ledger and vaccines and Mother and Child Health Booklet particularly for BCG vaccine..</li>
<li>Check Vaccine Vial Monitor for potency</li>
<li>If card is missing, in case of doubt, immunize. An extra dose will do no harm.</li>
<li>Immunize sick children, unless they are hospitalised. If so, immunize before they are discharged.</li>
<li>Administer measles vaccine to admitted children on discharge.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>open vaccine and immunize even one child to avoid missed opportunity</li>
<li>Don't schedule immunization sessions ie should 8-5pm Mon-Friday.</li>
<li>All the vaccines can be given safely the same day first doses as long as they are due.</li>
<li>Never give expired vaccines by checking expiry date.</li>
<li>Use one sterile AD syringe (non re-useable injection) and one sterile needle per injection.</li>
<li>Minimum interval between two doses of DPT/HepB+Hib OPV, and TT is 4 weeks.</li>
<li>All injectable vaccines must only be administered by duly registered clinicians/Nurses.</li>
<li>Reconstitution of all lyophilized (freeze dried) vaccines must only be done with their matching diluents as provided by the specific manufacturer.</li>
<li>All reconstituted multi-dose vial vaccines must be discarded after the manufacturer's prescribed maximum duration of use (normally 6 hours after reconstitution or opening).</li>
<li>All unused doses of a liquid multi-dose vial vaccine without a preservative must be discarded 6 hours after opening of the vial - e.g. multi-dose vials of liquid Pneumococcal Conjugate Vaccines.</li>
</ul>
<p>While MDVV eg TT,OPV,IPV must be discarded after 28days upon opening.</p>
<ul>
<li>Screening for immune status of individuals before administering the vaccine isn't required unless otherwise.</li>
<li>Ensure proper documentation on appropriate tools.</li>
<li>Check immunization status of any pregnant woman and women of child bearing age coming to MCH clinic, whatever the reason.</li>
<li>Check if the mother knows:</li>
<li>Which vaccine was given;</li>
<li>Which normal reactions are expected and what to do;</li>
<li>Next appointment date due</li>
<li>Record every vaccine given in the three places: documentation to follow.</li>
</ul>
<p>There is no maximum time interval between two doses. Even if a year passes between successive doses of vaccine, do not restart. However remember, interferes with the child is protection.</p>
<p>Child can receive all due doses in one day if first contact.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-kepi-vaccines">NON-KEPI VACCINES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-kepi-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cholera, typhoid, HePatitisA, B&amp;C, Rabies, Snake, influenza-H5N1, H1N1, Varicella-chiken pox, HPV</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="new-emerging-vaccines">NEW &amp; EMERGING VACCINES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#new-emerging-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="malaria-vaccine">Malaria vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malaria-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Current clinical studies have shown that new candidate vaccines can induce complete protection against malaria infection.</li>
<li>Complete protection against malaria can be induced by infecting volunteers with irradiated malaria parasites.</li>
<li>People living in endemic areas who have had multiple exposures to malaria develop immunity against severe malaria disease.</li>
<li>Since antibodies are unable to attack the malaria parasite once it has invaded liver cells, new approaches to the malaria vaccine development have been to design a vaccine that will induce potent T-cell responses against the liver stage of malaria infection.</li>
</ol>
<p>Preliminary Phase III clinical trial results for RTS,S/AS01 malaria vaccine indicate that it is about 50% efficacious with a protection of 12 months.</p>
<p>It is a Pre-erythrocytic stage vaccine candidate (liver stage).</p>
<p>WHO policy on malaria vaccine is expected by 2016.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hiv-vaccine">HIV vaccine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-vaccine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Despite the international community's best efforts- the HIV pandemic continues unabated.</p>
<p>In 2006, more than 39 million people were living with HIV worldwide. Over four million people became newly infected with HIV and an estimated 2.8 million lost their lives to AIDS.</p>
<p>Nearly 14,000 people become infected with HIV each day.</p>
<p>On average, people require life-saving antiretroviral treatment (ARVs) 7-10 years after becoming infected. While there has been recent progress in increasing access to treatment and prevention programs, HIV continues to outpace the global response with at least 80% of those in clinical need of ARVs worldwide not receiving them.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Further, while decline in national HIV prevalence has occurred in some sub-Saharan African countries, these trends are not strong or widespread enough to have a major impact on the epidemics.</p>
<p>New technologies to prevent HIV transmission remain imperative and the potential positive impact of AIDS vaccines would be enormous. An effective preventive HIV vaccine could prevent almost 30 million of the 150 million new infections projected in the coming decades.</p>
<p>There is scientific progress underway in the search for an HIV vaccine. Presently, there are more than 30 clinical trials with HIV vaccine candidates worldwide.</p>
<p><strong>An AIDS Vaccine</strong> would make a difference by:</p>
<ul>
<li>protecting vaccinated individuals against HIV infection</li>
<li>reducing the probability that a vaccinated individual who later becomes infected will transmit the infection to others; or</li>
<li>slowing the rate of progression to AIDS for those who later become infected with HIV.</li>
</ul>
<p>Currently, there is no licensed vaccine to protect against HIV/AIDS.</p>
<p>The preventive AIDS vaccines currently in human trials do not contain any live virus that could result in infection and thus cannot cause HIV/AIDS.</p>
<p>These vaccine candidates are recombinant vaccines that use genetically engineered components of HIV (i.e. contain only harmless particles or copies of particles of the virus—enough to trigger the body’s immune system, but not cause disease).</p>
<p><strong>Documentation tools used in monitoring performance.</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The permanent Register- TT, BCG, OPV, Penta, PCV10, Rota, measles.</li>
<li>The immunization tally sheet-for monthly report writing.</li>
<li>The immunization summary sheet-for monthly reporting to the sc office.</li>
<li>Immunization monitor chart-monitor performance as per immunization coverage. penta1-access and penta 3-utilization, Measles-fully immunized.</li>
<li>The Ante-natal Register for TT administered to pregnant women.</li>
<li>The TT injection register or booklet-register all daily TT administered as TT 1,2,3,4,5</li>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklet-follow up or TT Card.</li>
</ul>

</ul>

<li>Every vaccine transaction should be recorded thus: received, issued and returned on individual row.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">

</ol>
<p><strong>National Immunisation schedule</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A fully immunized child is one who has received all the prescribed antigens and at least one Vitamin A dose under the national immunization schedule before the first birthday.</li>
<li>A fully immunized person (other than an infant) refers to an individual who has received all the prescribed doses for a particular antigen eg TT, Hep B, Typhoid etc</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adverse-events-following-immunizations-aefis">ADVERSE EVENTS FOLLOWING IMMUNIZATIONS (AEFIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-events-following-immunizations-aefis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong> This is a reaction that occurs in a client/pt following vaccination that is considered to be related to the vaccine until proved otherwise.</p>
<ul>
<li>AEFIs may be classified as mild, moderate or severe.</li>
<li>AEFI occurs even in the most careful circumstances but only rarely is there a direct causal relationship between the vaccine and the adverse event.</li>
<li>AEFIs may be localized to the injection site or generalized to the whole body.</li>
<li>AEFIs may manifest immediately after vaccination or any time within 48 hours after vaccination.</li>
<li>Some AEFIs are recognized inherent side effects of vaccines e.g OPV and vaccine induced paralytic polio.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="possible-causes-of-aefi">Possible Causes of AEFI.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possible-causes-of-aefi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Programmatic errors: Usually they H/service provider based i.e. an error in handling, reconstitution or administration of the vaccine.</li>
<li>Nature of the vaccine (vaccine properties) or individual response to the vaccine itself.</li>
<li>Coincidental, is an event that has no causal association between the immunization and the medical condition of the child or woman.</li>
<li>Unknown cause. The cause of the event cannot be determined.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-aefis1">COMMON AEFIs1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-aefis1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Anaphylactic shock-sudden antibody-antigen reaction. Itchy, urticarial rash (in over 90% of cases)</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Progressive, painless swelling (angioedema) - face and the mouth, preceded by itchiness, tearing, nasal congestion or facial flushing.</p>
<ul>
<li>Respiratory symptoms - sneezing, coughing, wheezing, and laboured breathing; upper way swelling (indicated by hoarseness and/or difficulty swallowing) possibly causing airway obstruction</li>
<li>Hypotension, which generally develops later in the illness and can progress to cause shock and collapse.</li>
<li>Injection site abscesses - hard or soft swelling containing pus at inj site eg redness, painful.</li>
<li>BCG lymphadenitis - swollen cervical or armpit lymph nodes. c/picture of TB.</li>
<li>Deaths that are related to immunization.</li>
<li>Cases requiring admission/hospitalization that is related to immunization.</li>
<li>Other unusual or severe medical incidents that are thought by health workers or the public to be related to vaccination - convulsions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nb-non-significant-reaction-to-vaccines-includes">NB/Non-significant reaction to vaccines includes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb-non-significant-reaction-to-vaccines-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fever,</li>
<li>Redness or swelling at the injection site,</li>
<li>Rash.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-aefi-is-an-important-area-to-address-in-immunization">Why AEFI is an important Area to Address in Immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-aefi-is-an-important-area-to-address-in-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An AEFI may upset people to the extent that they refuse further immunizations for their children.</p>
<ul>
<li>Their refusal to accept the vaccine puts children at risk of vaccine-preventable diseases &amp; their consequences.</li>
<li>The health worker should be able to diagnose, treat and report all AEFIs.</li>
<li>The health worker should be able to urgently reassure the mother to allay anxiety to ensure continuity &amp; completion of vaccination.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immediate-steps">Immediate steps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-steps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take the affected child to the resuscitation room or a safe place away from the crowd &amp; give the correct treatment as per the condition.</li>
<li>Administer epinephrine 0.01 ml/kg (maximum 0.5 ml) of aqueous epinephrine 1:1000 by SC or IM injection in the limb (opposite limb to where the vaccination was given); speedy intervention is of paramount importance. Repeat at 20-minutes interval if necessary.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs and reassess the situation frequently, to guide medication use.</li>
<li>Ask or shout for help from colleagues</li>
<li>Re-assure the parent as the child gets treatment</li>
<li>Collect the vaccine vial and the diluent which were used and document the details (date of manufacture, expiry date, batch number and manufacturer)</li>
<li>Take a sample specimen as per the condition and take for laboratory analysis</li>
<li>Observe until the child’s condition improves. if the condition does not improve within 2 hours refer to the next level</li>
<li>Report the AEFI within 24 hours and investigate within 48 hours</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="long-term-steps">Long-term steps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-term-steps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Communicate to parents, community and public at large about AEFI’s and reassure them about immunization safety</li>
<li>Train all concerned persons as a corrective measure for the operational problem such as knowledge and skills gap</li>
<li>Conduct regular supportive supervision and give feedback</li>
<li>Improve availability of supplies and the working condition of the equipments to minimize program errors e.g. high</li>
</ol>
