<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="notification-of-an-adverse-event-following-immunization">Notification of an Adverse Event Following Immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#notification-of-an-adverse-event-following-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management-aefis">Management AEFIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-aefis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>What to notify</li>
<li>Who to notify</li>
<li>How to conduct the notification</li>
<li>How to preserve the evidence (vial/syringe etc.)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="steps">Steps:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Complete the official AEFI notification form within 48hrs as provided by DVI</li>
<li>Send 2 copies of the completed notification form to the DMOH’s office.</li>
<li>The DMOH sends one copy of the completed notification form to DVI</li>
<li>Note: because of the urgency of the investigations of an AEFI, the facility or the DMOH should call and alert DVI immediately an AEFI is detected.</li>
<li>Do not address the media without facts. Refer the media to the head, DVI</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-key-action-points-on-aefi">The key action points on AEFI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-key-action-points-on-aefi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To increase immunization acceptance and improve the quality of services through the proper surveillance of AEFIs by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Detecting and reporting AEFIs as they occur.</li>
<li>Investigating AEFIs when they occur.</li>
<li>Analyzing reports of AEFIs</li>
<li>Taking appropriate action following reports of AEFIs.</li>
<li>Evaluating the reporting system for AEFIs.</li>
<li>Preventing AEFIs in routine immunization and mass campaigns</li>
</ul>
<p>Supervision will greatly contribute to the reduction of this unwanted phenomenon.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-investigation">The purpose of investigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-investigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clarify the outcome of the medical incident/s</li>
<li>To identify the vaccine used (batch number, expiry date etc.)</li>
<li>To confirm whether a reported event was a single incident or a cluster.</li>
<li>To determine whether un-immunized people in the same area are experiencing the same medical incidents.</li>
<li>To allay the fears rumours immediate action is also important to assure members of the community that their health and concerns are taken seriously.</li>
<li>What data is required for AEFI case Investigation?</li>
</ul>
<p>For this purpose, analysis of data on AEFIs consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reviewing the case investigation report for each patient,</li>
<li>Other data about the event and the community in which it took place,</li>
<li>Reviewing laboratory results,</li>
<li>Making a final diagnosis, and identifying the probable cause.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-does-aefi-data-analyses-finding-solutions-to-it">Who does AEFI data Analyses/finding solutions to it?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-does-aefi-data-analyses-finding-solutions-to-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The h/worker who detects AEFI should analyses data at initial stage.</li>
<li>Epidemiologist</li>
<li>Clinician</li>
<li>Laboratory technician or</li>
<li>Disease Surveillance coordinator.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reducing-incidences-of-aefi">Reducing Incidences of AEFI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reducing-incidences-of-aefi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-contraindications-true">1. Contraindications - TRUE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-contraindications-true" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Client history for allergies and previous adverse reactions before administering vaccines.</li>
<li>In the case of a possible serious allergy, consult supervisor appropriate before giving vaccine.</li>
<li>Minimizes the occurrence of anaphylaxis but will not remove the risk altogether.</li>
<li>Low-grade fever, mild respiratory infections and other minor illnesses</li>
<li>Diarrhoea should not be considered a contraindication to OPV.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB/ It is particularly important to immunize children suffering from malnutrition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precaution-on-allergic-reactions-previously-experienced">Precaution on Allergic Reactions previously experienced<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precaution-on-allergic-reactions-previously-experienced" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Do not give the second or third DPT Hep+ Hib injection should not be given to a child who has suffered such a severe anaphylactic reaction to the previous dose. Because these events are so rare, it is not known which component of the combined DTP (or additional antigens in the combination vaccines) is responsible for allergic reactions. Therefore, no further dose of any of the vaccine components should be given unless assessment implicates the responsible antigen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="false-contraindications">False Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#false-contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Low-grade fever,</li>
<li>Mild respiratory infections and</li>
<li>Diarrhoea should not be considered a contraindication to OPV</li>
<li>Other minor illnesses eg mild children suffering from malnutrition.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-programme-error">2. Programme error<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-programme-error" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Improper handling of vaccines or faulty immunization technique, the actions to be taken will probably include one or more of the following:</li>
</ul>
<p>A. Logistics: Improving logistics will be the appropriate response if investigations indicate lack of supplies or equipment or failure of the cold chain.</p>
<p>H/workers should investigate suspected faults in the cold chain to find the cause and take appropriate measures.</p>
<p>The problem might be solved by providing additional equipment (needles, syringes, sterilizers, vaccine carriers, cold packs), vaccine or diluent.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Training: used to solve operational problems: lack of skills and knowledge &amp; poor attitude of H/ workers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Supervision: Non-serious AEFIs (e.g. abscesses) reported to the health facility should be able to alert the health worker to seek for the cause for immediate corrective action.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication: Health workers should inform parents and the community about AEFIs, and assure them of immunization safety.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Health workers should be prepared to respond quickly to rumours and public inquiries.</p>
<p>The key to maintaining confidence in health services is to be honest.</p>
<p>If the cause of the AEFI has not been identified, people should be told.</p>
<p>A vaccine-induced AEFI can be a sensitive communication problem.</p>
<p>The public needs to be assured that severe vaccine-induced events are rare, although this may not comfort the patient’s family.</p>
<p>The best that can be done is to show genuine sympathy and concern.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Evaluate the quality of AEFI surveillance regularly and should lead to remedial actions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-should-the-system-be-evaluated">How should the system be evaluated?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-should-the-system-be-evaluated" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Completeness, timeliness, and accuracy of reporting. Checking of the report receipt dates is also useful to districts and higher levels to monitor timeliness of reporting.</li>
<li>Accuracy. Health workers should periodically check the accuracy of routine disease surveillance reports and observe their work to make sure that recommended improvements have become a part of daily practice.</li>
</ul>
<p>DOWNGADED BY Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Swiftness. At the end of each AEFI investigation, the health worker should evaluate how quickly the response to the reported AEFI was done, using the following parameters:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whether the AEFI was reported within 24 hours of detection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whether an investigation begun within 48 hours after the report was received.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Appropriateness of actions taken to avoid further programme errors. Health should review case investigation and event description reports to see that the actions proposed for the elimination of programme errors are adequate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Participation in immunization programmes by communities. Over time, a good AEFI surveillance should result in an increase in immunization coverage due to increased community participation.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>If the health worker reduces the programme errors to a minimum or even to nil, if he or she takes immediate and appropriate measures when AEFI occurs:</p>
<ul>
<li>If communities are well informed on causes of AEFIs,</li>
<li>The confidence in immunization and in the staff will grow in the community, resulting in Increased participation.</li>
<li>Monthly AEFI surveillance reports, AEFI annual reports, and coverage data can done this assessment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disease-surveillance">DISEASE SURVEILLANCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease-surveillance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Define the term disease surveillance</li>
<li>Outline types of disease surveillance</li>
<li>Describe steps in EPI disease surveillance</li>
<li>Describe steps in investigation for the three EPI target diseases</li>
<li>Detect, investigate, report and respond to outbreaks of the three EPI target diseases</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-disease-surveillance">What is disease surveillance?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-disease-surveillance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The collection, analysis, &amp; interpretation of data to determine disease trends and patterns.</li>
<li>Enables managers to respond to existing problems &amp; take steps to prevent anticipated problems.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="it-provides-information-such-as">-It provides information such as:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-provides-information-such-as" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disease incidence, morbidity, and mortality, and progress in achieving disease control goals</li>
<li>Changes in patterns of morbidity and mortality among different age groups in different geographical areas &amp; among different economic, social, or cultural groups.</li>
<li>Impact of immunization strategies on disease incidence</li>
<li>Disease trends</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-disease-surveillance">Types of Disease Surveillance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-disease-surveillance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Facility-Based Routine Surveillance</strong>- health workers are required to report on the number of individuals that come to their facility and are diagnosed with notifiable diseases by detecting &amp; reporting information on diseases that bring patients to the h/facility is known as <strong>passive surveillance</strong> eg MOH 719.</p>
<p><strong>Community-Based Surveillance</strong> - properly trained community members can expand facility-based surveillance by detecting and reporting cases that may go undetected by the H/facility.</p>
<p><strong>Sentinel Surveillance (active surveillance)</strong> - is the collection and analysis of data by designated institutions selected for their geographic location, medical specialty, and ability to accurately diagnose and report high quality data.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surveillance-activities">Surveillance Activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surveillance-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Detection</li>
<li>Investigation</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Reporting</li>
<li>Analysis and interpretation</li>
<li>Presentation</li>
<li>Response</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="detection">Detection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#detection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Surveillance begins with case detection.</p>
<p>To accurately detect disease, health workers need case definitions that are appropriate for the local context, and they need practice in applying them, especially when they do not see a specific illness very often such as is the case of Polio.</p>
<p>Even with appropriate case definitions, clinical diagnoses can be a problem.</p>
<p>Many illnesses have similar symptoms, such as fever and rash, and can be differentiated only by laboratory tests that may not be accessible.</p>
<p>Each facility should have a disease surveillance focal person who should co-ordinate through availing the specimen collection tools, carry out Active Case Search and communicate to the SC Disease Surveillance Co-ordinator (SCDSC).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigation-and-reporting">Investigation and Reporting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigation-and-reporting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ministry of health through HMIS require that facilities routinely report the total count of cases of each reportable disease that has occurred within a specified time usually monthly in the MOH 719.</p>
<p>When no cases have occurred during the period, the report should indicate this fact (Zero report).</p>
<p>For EPI target diseases reporting is case based i.e each case should be reported individually using the IDSR form.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surveillance-and-data-flow-summary">Surveillance and Data Flow Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surveillance-and-data-flow-summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Health care facility</strong> (Detect, collect specimens, Investigate and respond)</p>
<p><strong>SC Health Office</strong> (collect specimens, investigate, Analyze, and respond)</p>
<p><strong>National Health Office</strong> (Investigate, analyze, and respond)</p>
<p><strong>Reporting Feedback</strong></p>
<p>Responses may include verification of reported cases, treatment, search for new cases, or supplemental vaccination activities, but all must be tailored to the disease and the situation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-coverage">IMMUNIZATION COVERAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-coverage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A measure of the extent to which the services being rendered cover the potential need for these services in the community on monthly basis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immunization coverage is the proportion of vaccinated individuals among the target popn.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most important indicators of a successful immunization programme.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Coverage is calculated by dividing the number of individuals vaccinated with a particular antigen (numerator) by the number of individuals targeted for vaccination with the antigen (denominator) within the same period.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This proportion is then multiplied by 100 to get %tage coverage.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-used-to-collect-and-analyze-data-on-immunization-coverage">Tools used to collect and analyze data on immunization coverage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-used-to-collect-and-analyze-data-on-immunization-coverage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Daily tally sheets; a sheet of paper used to count immunization given daily</li>
<li>Child immunization card: helps the mother to show return dates for next immunization</li>
<li>Monitor chart: illustrates progress of immunization coverage in community health centres</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Monthly immunization report: shows total immunizations given monthly to children under one year and pregnant mothers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-remedies-of-low-immunization-coverage">CAUSES/REMEDIES OF LOW IMMUNIZATION COVERAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-remedies-of-low-immunization-coverage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="missed-opportunities-for-immunization">Missed Opportunities for immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#missed-opportunities-for-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Occurs when any eligible child or woman comes to a health facility and does not receive any or all of the vaccine doses for which he or she is eligible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causes-missed-opportunities-for-immunization">Causes Missed Opportunities for immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-missed-opportunities-for-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Health facility does not offer immunization services</li>
<li>Health facility is experiencing vaccine stock-out</li>
<li>Health workers do not use appropriate (false) contraindications to immunizations</li>
<li>Health workers do not routinely screen children and women for their immunization status and offer the recommended vaccines</li>
<li>Health workers do not give all the vaccines for which the children and women are eligible at the time of the visit.</li>
<li>Health worker decides to schedule certain vaccines for fear of running out of vaccines or a high vaccine wastage (multi-dose liquid (lyophilized) vaccines)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ways-to-reduce-missed-opportunities">Ways to reduce missed opportunities:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ways-to-reduce-missed-opportunities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Conduct periodic surveys to measure missed opportunities</li>
<li>Examining health facility records and immunization cards (Child Health and Antenatal Cards)</li>
<li>Check immunization status of every child 0-23 months and pregnant women visiting health facilities or coming to the outreach site for any reason. Those in need should be immunized before leaving</li>
<li>Avoid false contraindications to immunization e.g. fever, cold, diarrhoea, vomiting and malnutrition.</li>
</ul>
<p>Incorrect use of contraindications denies life-saving immunizations to many infants</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure that all eligible women and children have an immunization card and that they bring the card to every clinic visit and that these cards are checked by the health worker on every visit and the relevant details discussed with the mother</li>
<li>Ensure children sick enough to be admitted are immunized on admission or before discharge from hospitals</li>
<li>Avoid scheduling of vaccination services and inconsistent outreaches</li>
<li>Encourage health workers to open a multi-dose vial of a lyophilised vaccine, even for one child.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary-of-indications-and-contraindications-to-epi-vaccines">Summary of Indications and Contraindications to EPI Vaccines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary-of-indications-and-contraindications-to-epi-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Immunize children who are malnourished</li>
<li>Immunize pregnant women with Tetanus Toxoid. However, because of the theoretical risk of teratogenicity, avoid giving the vaccine in early pregnancy.</li>
<li>Illnesses not requiring hospitalization are not contraindications for vaccination.</li>
<li>For children who have an illness requiring hospitalization defer vaccination until the condition of the child improves. Make sure that the child is vaccinated before being discharged. Do not give live vaccines (Yellow fever, Measles) to symptomatic HIV infected children.</li>
</ol>
<p>In HIV asymptomatic children, the measles vaccine should be given at six and nine months of age.</p>
<p>Do not give BCG to children who have symptomatic infection with HIV.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Do not immunize children who have had a previous severe event (reaction) after a previous dose of the vaccine</li>
</ol>
<p>Reducing missed opportunities is the cheapest way to increase coverage.</p>
<p>If the mother comes and no immunization is due this day, don't be angry, don't send her back. Explain why, tell her when the next immunization is, weigh and provide other services (e.g. check diet, give vitamin A, provide nutritional counselling etc) for the child or for her) so she doesn't feel she lost her time.</p>
<p>Drop out</p>
<p>A child who is legible for a particular antigen does not come back and complete subsequent immunizations.</p>
<p>Causes</p>
<ul>
<li>Health workers not explaining to women need to take immunization/ giving return dates</li>
<li>Lack of awareness leading to little social support</li>
<li>Health facilities opening at inconvenient time-late</li>
<li>Failure to follow immunization schedule</li>
<li>Unsympathetic health workers (poor service provider attitude)</li>
<li>Failure to return by women due to long cues</li>
<li>Change of residence-migration.</li>
<li>Vaccine stock outs</li>
</ul>
<p>Possible solutions to drop outs.</p>
<ul>
<li>Undertake social mobilization activities</li>
<li>Respond to community needs</li>
<li>Train health workers on appropriate proper immunization activities</li>
<li>Provide health education</li>
<li>Conduct local immunization days</li>
<li>Ensure continuous supply of vaccines</li>
<li>Open more outreach clinics to capture the hard to reach population</li>
</ul>
<p>Never reach children—Non immunized eligible children.</p>
<p>Causes</p>
<ul>
<li>Unaware of services availability</li>
<li>Don't value health services provided by the health centre.</li>
<li>Can't spare time to visit health centers coz they are busy</li>
<li>Lack of money</li>
<li>Believe that health services are harmful and costly</li>
<li>Cultural ethnic barriers/religion</li>
</ul>
<p>Solutions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Undertake social mobilization activities</li>
<li>Provide outreach services</li>
<li>Conduct local immunization days</li>
<li>Respond to community needs</li>
<li>Train community volunteers</li>
</ul>
<p>Lack of geographical access</p>
<ul>
<li>inability to access h/facility offering immunization services due to poor terrain.</li>
</ul>
<p>Causes</p>
<ul>
<li>Bad land terrain</li>
</ul>
<p>document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Floods
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Lack of resources to reach these people
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>≻</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\succ</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">≻</span></span></span></span></span> Lack of motivation to health workers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solutions">Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Obtain additional resources</li>
<li>Provide outreach</li>
<li>Offer motivation to workers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="increasing-maximizing-immunization-coverage">INCREASING / MAXIMIZING IMMUNIZATION COVERAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#increasing-maximizing-immunization-coverage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Limit missed opportunities by using MCBs, permanent register, false CIs, Use of MDVP.</li>
<li>Reduce drop outs by giving TCAs, exhibiting positive attitude, avoid long queues.</li>
<li>Defaulter tracing by use of PHTs, CHWS</li>
<li>Conducting routine immunization schedules and SIAs (campaigns)</li>
<li>Enough vaccine stocks in the facility &amp; buffer during stock out or shortage.</li>
<li>Communication for immunization services (Advocacy) &amp; community linkage through CHWs. Ensures community ownership &amp; utilization of immunization services.</li>
<li>Involve community in; planning, implementation &amp; monitoring of immunization services.</li>
<li>Monitoring for action to solve problems eg review meetings, supportive supervision &amp; peer review in the h/facilities.</li>
<li>Implementing govt policy on immunization; offering all vaccines daily from mon-Friday. Ensure 24hr access to emergency vaccines</li>
<li>Ensure FoC vaccination services in public and private H/Facilities.</li>
<li>Conduct outreach immunization activities especially hard to reach popns.</li>
<li>Poor documentation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organizing-and-conducting-an-immunization-session">Organizing and conducting an immunization session<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizing-and-conducting-an-immunization-session" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>ENSURE LONGISTICS IN PLACE - Working equipment, Electricity/Gas cylinder, vaccines in a carrier, accessories, H/service provider, safety boxes, waste bins &amp; records.</li>
<li>ARRANGEMENT OF SPACE FOR IMMUNIZATION</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Affects how you perform your work and the time taken by parent/guardian to during the immunization process.</li>
<li>The space that you set up for immunizations should be:</li>
<li>In a clean area not directly exposed to the sunlight, rain or drought.</li>
<li>Convenient for H/Worker who is offering vaccines and immunizing.</li>
<li>Easily accessible to parent/guardian, arranged with no crowding around the station.</li>
<li>Quiet enough for health workers to be able to explain what he or she is doing and give advice.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>ORGANIZING PATIENT / CLIENT FLOW</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Organize one way flow client flow to avoid overcrowding &amp; missed opportunities.</li>
<li>Immunization should be integrated with other MCH services for good patient / guardian flow.</li>
<li>For smooth floor two doors are ideal; entry and the other exit.</li>
<li>Improvise in case of single door by h/workers local arrangement.</li>
<li>Greet &amp; welcome the mothers in a friendly way.</li>
<li>New parents/guardian’s, issue them appropriate cards and fill in bio data.</li>
<li>For re-attendants (clients), tick in the appropriate registers.</li>
<li>Guide the parent / guardian into a single queue to enter the MCH area.</li>
<li>Ensure a first-come first served system.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>As far as possible try to see one parent/ guardian at a time.</li>
<li>Children who are very sick should be identified and attended to first (filtering).</li>
<li>When the parents/guardians are through at MCH clinic, thank them for coming &amp; give TCA.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-health-facility-should-have-the-following-requirements">The Health facility should have the following requirements:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-health-facility-should-have-the-following-requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Waiting area - sit before being immunized as they receive health talks; as the talks will be better received if people are comfortably seated in the waiting bay.</li>
<li>Space and equipment’s for screening - weighing scales, registration, recording and immunizing.</li>
<li>A table or stools for vaccines and injection equipment’s.</li>
<li>Two chairs/stools; health worker &amp; parent or guardian.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="points-to-remember-in-mch">Points to remember in MCH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-remember-in-mch" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep vaccines cold in a refrigerator and maintain +2oc to +8oc.</li>
<li>Keep the refrigerator closed all the time.</li>
<li>Remove from refrigerator all vaccines needed for the session using a vaccine carrier.</li>
<li>Ensure that the vaccine carriers are closed all the time.</li>
<li>Change the ice pack before temperature reach +80 c.</li>
<li>Be friendly to both the parents/guardians and children.</li>
<li>Check all children to see what immunizations they have had and what they are due for.</li>
<li>If in doubt, ask the parents/guardians and confirm from the card.</li>
<li>Tell mothers about the reaction to expect from immunizations.</li>
</ul>
<p>Many mothers may have heard rumors.</p>
<p>Reassure and tell them what to expect and how to respond.</p>
<ul>
<li>Remember: Injectable immunizations need sterile procedures.</li>
<li>Ensure your equipment i.e. AD syringes, reconstitution syringes and safety boxes are available and properly assembled.</li>
<li>Use only one sterile syringe and needle for each injection.</li>
</ul>
<p>After use, dispose it into safety box immediately at the point of use.</p>
<ul>
<li>After the clinic session, take all tally sheets and fill in the monthly summary sheet.</li>
</ul>
<p>Clean and tidy up the clinic before you go off duty, ready for the next day.</p>
<ul>
<li>Offer immunization services from 8am-5pm Monday to Friday.</li>
<li>Get vaccines from the fridge and all relevant documentation is done.</li>
<li>Open antigen immediately the first child arrives.</li>
<li>If/educate the mother of the child on importance of completing immunization and expected reaction.</li>
<li>Always give the mother of the child Return date for the next visit (document).</li>
<li>Discard lyophilized, freezed vaccines after 6 hours and return Multi dose vaccine vial to the refrigerator if meets WHO re-use criteria.</li>
<li>Document all relevant information.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="planning-and-implementing-services-with-the-community">Planning and Implementing Services with the Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#planning-and-implementing-services-with-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health staff should maintain a permanent dialogue and partnership with community leaders and caregivers in order to increase and sustain their support and participation in the immunization program and to enhance their understanding of the importance and timely completion of the vaccination schedule.</p>
<p>Share your achievements with the community: inform people on how many children you have immunized each month and the number of cases of target diseases that have decreased compared to the previous years.</p>
<p>Also communicate programme needs: tracking for pregnant women and newborns, support for ensuring outreach and reducing drop-outs.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>A</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Be sure to coordinate with your Community Health Workers and/or Community Health Educator to help dissemination information and communicate with clients and the community.</p>
<p>Although knowledge per se is insufficient to create demand, poor knowledge about vaccination is a good predictor of poor compliance. Children do not get vaccinated if caregivers do not know the value of vaccines, when children need to be immunized, where vaccines are available, the appropriate series of vaccines to be followed, or the schedule for immunization. Health workers and Community Health Educators are encouraged to learn what community leaders and caregivers know and feel about the services.</p>
<p>The type of information that is communicated and the channels</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-community-health-workers">Role of Community Health Workers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-community-health-workers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Trained community health workers, health educators, and NGO partners can participate in increasing awareness of preventive services like immunization.</li>
<li>They can also assist with tracking defaulters, participate in outreach, &amp; mobilize households for health sessions.</li>
<li>The coverage area for each mobilizer or volunteer should be based on an analysis of the number and location of households that one mobilizer can feasibly reach.</li>
<li>Maintain cold chain hence ensuring potent vaccines administered.</li>
<li>Monitor functioning of equipment by identifying gaps</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tasks-carried-out-by-community-mobilizers">Tasks carried out by community mobilizers:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tasks-carried-out-by-community-mobilizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Identify target populations in catchment area</li>
<li>Prepare a list of assigned households with names of infants and mothers (including newborns and pregnant women)</li>
<li>Share lists of names with health workers to include in vaccination registers</li>
<li>Make home visits to encourage participation in fixed and outreach sessions</li>
<li>Help mothers to interpret immunization cards (Mother and Child Health Booklets and women’s TT doses)</li>
<li>Cooperate with the health worker to keep a track of infants and mothers who need to complete the immunization series</li>
<li>Follow up on defaulters tracing.</li>
<li>Provide information on the session dates and times and vaccination schedules.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cold-chain-system">COLD CHAIN SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-chain-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Define the cold chain system.</li>
<li>List the cold chain equipment used in the country.</li>
<li>Demonstrate packing of vaccines in the cold chain equipment.</li>
<li>Describe basic principles of refrigeration.</li>
<li>Discuss equipment installation procedure.</li>
<li>Monitor cold chain temperature.</li>
<li>Carry out preventive maintenance activities.</li>
<li>Conduct basic fault finding procedure and remedial action.</li>
<li>Be able to order spare parts.</li>
<li>Be able to take equipment inventory.</li>
<li>Know common cold chain emergencies.</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">DEFINITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Process of maintaining vaccines potency&amp;safety from the manufacturer to the recipient at SDP (child and woman of child bearing age).</li>
<li>Vaccines lose their potency when exposed to; high temperature, sunlight or freezing conditions depending on type.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-elements-of-cold-chain-system">Components/Elements of cold chain system.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-elements-of-cold-chain-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>People/personnel- to manage and distribute vaccines/cold chain equipment</li>
<li>Equipments-for storing and transporting vaccines</li>
<li>Maintaining of equipments-handling</li>
<li>Monitoring of equipments-if operational</li>
<li>Logistics-transport system-airroplane, vehicles</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-cold-chain">Principles of cold chain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-cold-chain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep vaccines cold and out of sunlight</li>
<li>Effective distribution of vaccines.</li>
<li>Maintain functional equipments</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2d7e0e66.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>shows how supplies of vaccines travel in cold chain links from the manufacturer to the central vaccine store and eventually to the recipient through the regional and district vaccine depots and finally to the immunizing health facility.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>An efficient cold chain system requires trained and skilled staff, reliable equipment and adherence to set standards.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-38e2d9e8.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg">
Fig 4.2 Vaccine Delivery System</p>
<p>The supply chain must deliver the right vaccines in the right place, at the right time, in the right quantities, in the right condition, at the right cost.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cold-chain-equipments-used-to-maintain-normal-temps">COLD CHAIN EQUIPMENTS USED TO MAINTAIN NORMAL TEMPS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-chain-equipments-used-to-maintain-normal-temps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Cold rooms and freezer rooms-at central/regional stores.</li>
<li>Freezers and Ice-lined refrigerators-sub county stores</li>
<li>Gas electric refrigerators</li>
<li>Solar Refrigerators-rural H/facilities.</li>
<li>Vaccine carriers</li>
<li>Cold boxes</li>
<li>Icepacks</li>
<li>Thermometers/fridge tag thermometer.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cold-rooms-and-freezer-rooms">Cold Rooms and Freezer Rooms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-rooms-and-freezer-rooms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Large rooms specially constructed for storage of large quantities of vaccines.</li>
<li>They have two cooling units; one running while the other is standby, a 24-hour temperature monitoring system with an alarm, a recorder, and a backup generator that will turn on automatically when the regular power is interrupted.</li>
<li>Found at the national and regional levels while freezer rooms are only found at the national level.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arranging-vaccines-in-refrigerators">Arranging vaccines in refrigerators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arranging-vaccines-in-refrigerators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Arrangement should facilitate air circulation and the reading of their identification and expiry date.</li>
<li>Vaccines whose expiry date is closest must be used first (First Expired, First out (FEFO/FIFO) principle).</li>
<li>Expire vaccines should not be preserved.</li>
<li>Opened and partially used vials of vaccines that satisfy the MDVP requirements brought back from an immunization session should be marked arranged separately.</li>
<li>To be used first in the next session.</li>
<li>The refrigerator with vaccines should only be opened in case of necessity (twice daily M/E).</li>
<li>Leaving the refrigerator open for too long must be avoided by all means.</li>
<li>Vaccine arrangement in the refridge should follow guidelines-high-low heat/cold sensitivity.</li>
<li>The arrangement for Health facility should follow the sensitivity of the vaccines to heat.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gas-electric-refrigerators">Gas Electric refrigerators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gas-electric-refrigerators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are currently three major types of gas electric refrigerators used in the country; these are</p>
<p>Sibir 170GE, RCW42EG and RCW50EG available on</p>
<p>5</p>

<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e6b6490e.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6cba5215.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p>-Vaccines are placed in shelves in order of sensitivity with the most sensitive to heat (OPV) being on the first shelf below the evaporator.</p>
<p>-TT and DPT+HepB –HiB being most sensitive to freezing are placed on the second last shelf from the bottom. -Vaccines are packed leaving space of about 5cm in between the packets for air circulation.</p>
<p>=The upper cabinet is used for freezing of icepacks.</p>
<p>This fridge is used at the SCounty vaccine store and at the immunizing facilities with high target population.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-principles-of-refrigeration">BASIC PRINCIPLES OF REFRIGERATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-principles-of-refrigeration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="terminologies">Terminologies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Refrigeration - The process of removing heat from an insulated space to maintain cold temperature.</li>
<li>Refrigerator - This is an airtight equipment connected to a power source which can either be gas or electricity to achieve cooling.</li>
<li>Refrigerant - A fluid with low boiling point which circulates in the refrigeration system to facilitate cooling.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-refrigeration-systems-used-in-epi">Types of refrigeration systems used in EPI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-refrigeration-systems-used-in-epi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Compression system</li>
<li>Absorption system</li>
</ul>
<p>Compression type: This type of refrigeration system uses a compressor, which when connected to electricity pumps the refrigerant through the pipes.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The pipes connect the inside of the refrigerator to the outside.</p>
<p>As the refrigerant circulates, it absorbs heat from inside lowering the temperature inside the refrigerator.</p>
<p>The refrigerator hums when in operation.</p>
<p>An example of this refrigerator is TCW 1152</p>
<p><strong>Absorption type:</strong> This type of refrigerator has a heating unit, which uses either gas or electricity.</p>
<p>When the heating unit is supplied with a source of heat the refrigerant boils, evaporates and circulates through the coiled pipes where it loses heat changing into liquid as it enters the pipe inside the refrigerator.</p>
<p>Due to the low boiling properties of the refrigerant it evaporates again as it enters the inside pipes and this results into cooling.</p>
<p>Absorption refrigerator is quiet when in operation.</p>
<p>An example of absorption type of refrigerator is RCW 42 EG.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cold-box">Cold Box<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-box" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cold boxes are normally used for transportation of vaccines.</p>
<p>They can also be used for temporary storage when a refrigerator breaks down.</p>
<p>The cold life of a cold box varies depending on the type, the number of openings and the ambient temperature.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vaccine-carriers">Vaccine Carriers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-carriers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>used to transport vaccines from SCounty stores to service delivery points (fixed, outreach / mobile-campaigns) and during immunisation sessions. The cold life in a vaccine carrier is approximately 8 hours.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-da3093f8.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="icepacks">Icepacks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#icepacks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Icepacks are flat rectangular plastic containers filled with water or gel.</li>
<li>They are used in vaccine carriers, cold boxes or refrigerators to maintain temperatures.</li>
<li>Always have at least an extra set of icepacks as a reserve while one set is in use.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thermometers">Thermometers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thermometers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>used to monitor cold chain temperature.
These are the dial and alcohol thermometers as shown below.
They indicate the safe operating ranges of temperature of btn +2 to +8OC for refrigerators &amp; -15 to -25OC for freezers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-fridge-thermometers">Types of fridge thermometers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-fridge-thermometers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fridge-tag">Fridge tag-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fridge-tag" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
