<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monitoring-cold-chain-temperature">MONITORING COLD CHAIN TEMPERATURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-cold-chain-temperature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-use-the-cold-chain-temperature-monitoring-chart">How to use the cold chain temperature-monitoring chart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use-the-cold-chain-temperature-monitoring-chart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Read and record the refrigerator temperature twice daily, morning and evening including Weekends &amp; public holidays.</p>
<p>Carefully record these temperature readings on the cold chain recording sheet.</p>
<p>You must enter:</p>
<ul>
<li>Name and type of refrigerator</li>
<li>Name of the district</li>
<li>Name of the health institution</li>
<li>Power Source (Normally operating on)</li>
<li>The date</li>
<li>The number of icepacks frozen today</li>
<li>The number of icepacks used today</li>
<li>The number of hours of electricity failure</li>
<li>Shortage of gas (Mark with X)</li>
<li>Gas cylinder renewed (Mark with X)</li>
<li>Plot the temperature morning and evening</li>
<li>Report on faults and problems at the bottom off the chart</li>
<li>Note that the bold line is for start of the day which is mid night and the broken line mid day.</li>
<li>Charting should therefore be done at the centre of the bold and dotted line in the morning, and at the centre of the broken and bold line for the evening charting.</li>
</ul>
<p>PREVENTIVE MAINTENANCE ACTIVITIES (Role of nurse in cold chain)</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5 studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="daily-activities">Daily activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Check temperature twice, in the morning and evening including public holidays and weekends and chart on the temperature-monitoring chart.
Ensure the temperature is between +2°C to +8°C.</li>
<li>Check that the refrigerator is operating and the burner flame is blue for gas refrigerator.</li>
<li>Make sure that there is enough gas in the cylinder.
Health worker should know how long a cylinder takes when running continuously.</li>
<li>Ensure that vaccines are well arranged in the refrigerator</li>
<li>DO NOT keep any other item in refrigerator apart from vaccines and diluents.</li>
<li>Keep a spare gas cylinder available and always replace the gas cylinder before it is completely empty.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="weekly-activities">Weekly activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weekly-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Check the ice formation on the evaporator. If the ice is thicker than 6mm to 10mm, defrost the refrigerator.</li>
<li>Check that the refrigerator is level.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monthly-activities">Monthly activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monthly-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Check that the condenser and cooling unit are clean. Remove any dirt or dust with a soft brush or cloth.</li>
<li>When necessary, clean inside and outside of the refrigerator with a damp cloth.</li>
<li>Clean door gasket and powder it with perfume free talcum.</li>
<li>Check the gas connections for leaks</li>
<li>In solar refrigerator</li>
<li>Gently wash the panels with plenty of water and soft cloth (avoid use of detergents)</li>
<li>Check battery acid level and top up with distilled water when necessary.</li>
<li>Check battery terminal for tightness and corrosion. Lubricate with battery terminal jelly or petroleum jelly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="824207d0">Yearly activities – by the medical engineering technician<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#824207d0" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Clean the gas burner and gas jet</li>
<li>Clean the flue and baffle</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-to-do-if-the-refrigerator-is-not-working-properly">WHAT TO DO IF THE REFRIGERATOR IS NOT WORKING PROPERLY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do-if-the-refrigerator-is-not-working-properly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The refrigerator is not working properly if any of the following happens:</p>
<ul>
<li>The refrigerator is not cooling at all</li>
<li>The refrigerator is not cold enough above 8 degrees centigrade</li>
<li>The refrigerator is too cold below 2 degrees centigrade</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="follow-these-follow-these-instructions-when-using-the-fault-finding-flow-chart-fig-4-19">Follow these Follow these instructions when using the fault finding flow chart fig 4.19<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#follow-these-follow-these-instructions-when-using-the-fault-finding-flow-chart-fig-4-19" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ensure that Vaccines are transferred into a vaccine carrier or cold box before determining the fault.</p>
<ul>
<li>Always start with the first possible fault as shown on the flow diagram.</li>
<li>Make sure that a fault does not exist before going on to the next one.</li>
<li>If, after checking all the possible faults, the refrigerator is still not working properly, start at the beginning and check everything again.</li>
<li>If, after checking all the possible faults twice, the refrigerator is not working properly, refer to the Sub county for further action by a trained technician</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="checking-the-door-sealing">Checking the door sealing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#checking-the-door-sealing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Place a thin paper (foolscap) strip in between the door and body of refrigerator</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="checking-gas-supply">Checking gas supply<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#checking-gas-supply" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Always keep a spare gas supply tube.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use soapy water to check for any gas leakage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is a leakage in the gas supply tube, replace it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Does not use the refrigerator on gas operation if there is leaking connections, which you cannot repair, refer to the district for further action by a skilled technician.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="checking-the-gas-thermostat">Checking the gas thermostat<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#checking-the-gas-thermostat" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Remove the capillary tube end from the evaporator.</li>
<li>Put the capillary tube end into a glass of ice cubes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="defrosting-of-the-fridge">Defrosting of the fridge<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#defrosting-of-the-fridge" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Put the vaccines into another fridge or cold box with frozen ice packs.</li>
<li>Take out ice trays</li>
<li>Turn off the refrigerator</li>
<li>When the ice is melted, wipe the evaporator shelf dry and the inside of the box with soap and warm water</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: do not use any sharp instrument to remove ice</p>
<p>Light the burner/plug it to the socket</p>
<p>Wait until temperature is +2 degree celcius then replace the vaccines and close the door</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cold-chain-emergencies">COLD CHAIN EMERGENCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cold-chain-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Emergencies can interrupt immunization services if not planned for.</p>
<p>Some of the common cold chain emergencies include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Equipment breakdown.</li>
<li>Electric power failure (black out).</li>
<li>Shortage of gas.</li>
<li>Shortage of spare parts.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="storage-and-transportation-of-vaccines-diluents">Storage and transportation of vaccines&amp; diluents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage-and-transportation-of-vaccines-diluents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>At all stages of vaccine transportation a cold chain monitor must always accompany all vaccines whether in cold boxes, vaccine carriers or portable fridges and the temperature reading must be maintained between +2°C and +8°C at all times using conditioned ice packs.</li>
<li>Diluents need not be transported at +2°C-+8°C unless they are being transported for outreach activities.</li>
<li>At regional or Scounty stores, diluents do not need to be stored in refrigerator or freezer, and should NEVER be frozen.</li>
<li>They must however be cooled to between +2°C &amp; +8°C before reconstitution.</li>
<li>This prevents thermal shock to the vaccine hence potency loss due to warm diluent.</li>
</ul>
<p>However, at facility level, all diluents must be stored in the vaccine refrigerator and in the same tray as their respective vaccines.</p>
<p>Diluents supplied with vaccines are specific for the vaccine, since they contain certain chemicals to stabilize the vaccine or potentiate the immune response, or protect the reconstituted vaccine from bacterial contamination.</p>
<p>It is essential that diluents are stored, distributed and used correctly.</p>
<p>Incorrect handling of diluents may cause adverse events following vaccination.</p>
<p>The disposal of expired and damaged vaccines shall be done according to MOH guidelines for disposal of all other drugs and related biological.</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monitoring-the-use-of-vaccines-to-maintain-potency">MONITORING THE USE OF VACCINES TO MAINTAIN POTENCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-the-use-of-vaccines-to-maintain-potency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a. Interpreting vaccine monitoring indicators
b. Multi-Dose Vial Policy (MDVP)
c. Monitoring vaccine use and vaccine wastage</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-interpreting-vaccine-monitoring-indicators">A. Interpreting vaccine monitoring indicators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-interpreting-vaccine-monitoring-indicators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The tools for monitoring vaccine exposure to high temperatures are:
i. Vaccine vial monitors (VVM)</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5fd86763.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<p>The white label is a heat-sensitive material, which is placed on a vaccine vial to register cumulative heat exposure over time.</p>
<p>The inner square is made of heat sensitive material, which is a lighter in color than the outer circle at the starting point and becomes darker with exposure to heat. Stage 1 no cause of alarm, 2 use urgently while stages 3&amp;4 don't use lost potency. Before opening a vial, the status of the VVM must be checked to see whether the vaccine has been damaged by heat.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>ii. 3M monitor</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Vaccine Cold Chain Monitor</th><th></th><th></th><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Date in</td><td>Index</td><td>Location</td><td></td><td>Date out</td><td>Index</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>To Activate</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Fold Up &amp; <ul>
<li>The monitor card must always be stored together with the vaccines throughout the cold chain system from the supplier to the central store, to the Scounty stores, to the health centre.</li>
<li>It detects cumulative heat exposure above 10oc and any exposure over 34oc. The explanation of what is required to be done is indicated on both sides of this card.</li>
<li>Mainly used in regional &amp;Sc vaccine stores and high voluminous H/facilities.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The tools for monitoring vaccine exposure to freezing are:</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Freeze watch indicator – mainly in the regional and central vaccine stores.</p>
<ul>
<li>Tells you when the vaccine has been exposed to freezing temperatures.</li>
<li>There two types of freeze watch indicators; pentavalent and TT vaccines.</li>
<li>A small vial containing blue (pentavalent) or red (TT) alcohol which is trapped inside a plastic bulbous tube with a white paper background.</li>
<li>When exposed to temperatures below 0°C for more than one hour, the vial bursts and releases the coloured liquid, staining the white paper background.</li>
<li>The freeze indicator is used to warn of freezing and is packed with vaccines that are sensitive to freezing temperatures, the vial breaks and releases a bright blue or red stain which spreads across the white paper background and the colour change cannot be reversed.</li>
</ul>
<p>The figure below shows the indicator with an unbroken vial and a broken vial.</p>
<p>If the paper background of the indicator is stained blue or red, the shake test should be performed.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a303e412.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-01b59300.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p>After freezing for over one hour, the indicator has burst out and has stained the background red. This shows that the temperature has been below 0°C.</p>
<p>b) Shake taste</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is a test used for testing suspected frozen vaccine vials.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>By shaking the vial it can be easily established whether vaccines TT&amp; pentavalent are frozen or not.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If suspected to been frozen, it is recommended to apply a shake test as follows:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take a vial you think may be frozen (Test sample)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Select another vial of the same type of vaccine that you know has not been frozen (control sample)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hold in one hand and shake vigorously for 10-15 seconds</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allow to stand and leave both vials to rest for 15-30 minutes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compare both vials against the light to see the sedimentation rate</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Results</p>
<ul>
<li>If the test sample shows a much slower sedimentation rate same as the control sample, the test sample has not been frozen.</li>
<li>If the sedimentation rate is faster and a thick sediment forms at the bottom of the vials, the test</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>sample has been damaged by freezing the supervisor should be notified.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="shake-test">Shake test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shake-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3fad2f0e.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vaccine-storage-conditions">Vaccine storage conditions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-storage-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  Vaccines | National
Up to 6 months,
(Electricity) | Sub National

<p>TT, liquid DPT+ Hepatitis B, PCV10 vaccines and diluents must NOT be frozen. Preparing vaccines for transportation from District by Health Facility</p>
<p>Conditioned icepacks should be used to transport vaccines in the vaccine carrier.</p>
<p>The vaccines should be arranged as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vials with YF, OPV and measles, BCG (LAV) vaccines and diluents placed at the bottom.</li>
<li>The; PCV10, Pentavalent, TT &amp; IPV vials will be placed at the top.</li>
<li>Vaccines must always be accompanied by diluents from the same supplier</li>
<li>Diluents used are for different antigens (BCG, measles and Yf vaccines) and from different Suppliers and they should not be interchanged because they made differently.</li>
<li>Diluents should be stored next to their respective vaccines or placed in the refrigerator, the day before use, in order to cool them before reconstitution to avoid thermal shock to vaccines.</li>
</ul>
<p>B. VACCINES OPEN VIAL POLICY- MDVV-Liquid vaccines.</p>
<p>A vial containing several doses of vaccine from which one or more doses have been taken.</p>
<p>The policy determines:</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>Studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i. Which of the opened vaccine vials may be preserved at the end of an immunization session and used the following days and
ii. The conditions under which these vaccines may be stored and re-used without any risk.</p>
<ul>
<li>MOH adopted WHO policy of using selected vaccines in subsequent immunization sessions</li>
<li>Eg liquid preparation (opened multi-dose vials); preservatives; OPV, TT, Hep B&amp; Penta.</li>
<li>Vaccines contain special preservatives assuring stability to heat and long lasting potency.</li>
<li>Also prevent or reduce bacterial contamination in the vials.</li>
</ul>
<p>ASSIGNMENT; Components of vaccine; Antigen, diluent, adjuvants, stabilizers, preservatives.</p>
<ul>
<li>MDVV have more doses to be removed during an immunization session &amp; used during subsequent immunization sessions for a maximum of 4 weeks provided the following criteria are met:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>The expiry date has not passed.</li>
<li>The vaccines are stored under appropriate cold chain conditions.</li>
<li>The vaccine vial septum has not been submerged in water.</li>
<li>Aseptic techniques have been used to withdraw all doses.</li>
<li>The Vaccine Vial Monitor (VVM) has not reached the discard point. (Stages 3&amp;4)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The policy on the re-use of opened multi-dose vials of vaccines applies to vaccine vials for use both in static or fixed as well as outreach vaccination sessions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All multi-dose liquid vaccines that are not likely to be exhausted in one or more vaccination schedules should be clearly labeled with the date when they were opened before they are returned to the vaccine refrigerator.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The policy for all freeze dried or lyophilized vaccines eg BCG, measles &amp; yellow fever once reconstituted, vials must be discarded at the end of each immunization session or at the end of 6 hours, whichever comes first.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-monitoring-the-vaccine-use-and-vaccine-wastage-rates">C. MONITORING THE VACCINE USE AND VACCINE WASTAGE RATES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-monitoring-the-vaccine-use-and-vaccine-wastage-rates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It ensures the quality of immunization services and keeps the vaccine wastage under control. The goals of the monitoring are two:</p>
<ol>
<li>To detect management problems and find appropriate solutions during the vaccine use</li>
<li>To contribute to the planning by providing data on vaccines needs and vaccines wastage rates</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaccine-wastage-and-use-rates">Vaccine wastage and use rates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-wastage-and-use-rates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The quantity of vaccine taken out of the stocks, but not administered to the target population.</li>
<li>The number of vaccine doses used is lower/higher than the number of individuals immunized.</li>
<li>The number of doses in excess represents "lost doses" or vaccine wastage.</li>
<li>Vaccines management should endeavor to avoid vaccine losses and minimize sacrificed doses.</li>
<li>This can be achieved only when the use of vaccines is efficiently monitored.</li>
</ul>
<p>Two types of vaccines wastage: - Total amount of wasted and sacrificed doses.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-wasted-doses-of-doses-in-unopened-vials-wastage-due-to-the-system">1. Wasted doses of doses in unopened vials (wastage due to the system)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-wasted-doses-of-doses-in-unopened-vials-wastage-due-to-the-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>unopened vials that have been lost before they could be administered for various reasons:</li>
<li>Poor handling of vaccines expiring while in the fridge.</li>
<li>Damaged vaccines due to freezing</li>
<li>Doses spoilt due to system failure e.g. VVM or 3 monitor reached discard point, breakdown in the cold chain, frozen DTP+ HepB and TT or removed labels.</li>
<li>Doses that have been lost during the administration of vaccines due to lack of skill or knowledge of the vaccinator (overdose, multi-dose vials that are thrown away by either mistake or non-adherence to the multi-dose vial policy, etc.).</li>
<li>Doses from vials broken during transport and handling (Accidents)</li>
<li>Missing doses from vaccine stock ledgers due to poor documentation</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Sacrificed doses in opened vials; for a good cause.</li>
</ol>
<p>Doses of vaccines lost deliberately for the sake of the immunization to take place</p>
<ul>
<li>The vials containing reconstituted vaccines that have been thrown away at the end of the immunization session in line with the MDVP.</li>
<li>The vaccines doses that have been administered to persons outside the target population</li>
</ul>
<p>The vaccine wastage rate is an indicator of the quality of immunization services.</p>
<p>The calculation of wastage rates is based on vaccines stock management information which must be accurate and reliable.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaccine-wastage-rate-and-wastage-factor">Vaccine wastage rate and wastage factor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-wastage-rate-and-wastage-factor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Doses used include -vaccines administered doses received by the targeted group
-wasted &amp; sacrificed doses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example-on-wastage-rate">Example on wastage rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-on-wastage-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rioma health facility had 200 doses of BCG vaccine in the month of July 2005 and immunized 150 children under one year.</p>
<p>To calculate the vaccine wastage rate for Rioma health facility using the formula is as follows: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>200</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>150</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>100</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>50</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">200 - 150 \times 100 = 50</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">200</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">150</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">50</span></span></span></span></span> Divided by <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>200</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>100</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>25</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">200 \times 100 = 25\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">200</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">25%</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wastage-factor">Wastage Factor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wastage-factor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vaccines Wastage Factor is a multiplier used to order vaccines to cater for the targeted popn &amp;wastage. The total number of vaccines supplied within given period is referred to as 100% supply.</p>
<p>Formula for calculating wastage factor</p>
<p><strong>100% supply Divide by (100% supply - Wastage Rate = Wastage Factor</strong></p>
<p>Using Rioma Health Facility example the wastage Factor is calculated as follows:</p>
<p>100 divided by <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>100</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>25</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mn>100</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(100 - 25) = 100</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">100</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">25</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span></span></span></span></span> divided <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>75</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>1.33</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">75 = 1.33</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">75</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1.33</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>In other terms, for every dose of a given antigen in the immunization schedule, we must anticipate 1.33 doses to take account of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>25</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">25%</span></span></span></span></span> wastage in the use of the vaccine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="documenting-vaccine-wastage">Documenting vaccine wastage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#documenting-vaccine-wastage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All immunizing facilities should document their vaccine wastage per antigen.</p>
<p>The tool for documenting vaccines wastage in each health facility is the monthly report.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-used-in-vaccine-management-wastages">Tools used in vaccine management &amp;Wastages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-used-in-vaccine-management-wastages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-vaccine-order-sheet">1. Vaccine Order Sheet<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-vaccine-order-sheet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Is useful tool that helps in ensuring that the min / max stocking policy is adhered to by the Health facility when placing the orders for vaccines.</li>
</ul>
<p>It should have the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Minimum and maximum stock</li>
<li>Number of children immunized</li>
<li>Available stock</li>
<li>Ordered vaccines</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="steps-in-ordering-vaccines">STEPS IN ORDERING VACCINES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-ordering-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Defining vaccine supply period</li>
<li>Calculating quantities of vaccine for a supply period</li>
<li>Calculating minimum stock level</li>
<li>Calculating maximum stock level</li>
<li>Calculating total quantities of vaccine to be ordered</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages-of-ordering-vaccines">ADVANTAGES OF ORDERING VACCINES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-ordering-vaccines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>a. Prevent vaccine stock outs and overstocking
b. Prevent expiry of vaccine during their storage</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>c. Ensures accessory supplies are "bundled" e.i. Safety boxes, syringes and needles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="controlling-vaccine-stocks">CONTROLLING VACCINE STOCKS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#controlling-vaccine-stocks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Receiving delivered vaccines and supplies</li>
<li>Storage, transport and handling of vaccines</li>
<li>Organizing vaccine distribution</li>
<li>Inventory of vaccine stocks</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-issue-voucher-s-11">2. Issue Voucher (S 11)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-issue-voucher-s-11" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A government requisition form which should be issued in two copies.</li>
<li>The original will be recorded and filed by the vaccine store manager.</li>
<li>The copy will be for the facility serve as acknowledgement of receipt the vaccines and other supplies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-vaccine-stock-ledger">3. Vaccine stock ledger.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-vaccine-stock-ledger" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>used in the store for recording vaccine movements to or from the refrigerator.</li>
<li>They should be kept with the vaccines on the same premises.</li>
<li>Every vaccine transaction should be recorded own booklet as:</li>
<li>Received, issued and returned on individual row.</li>
<li>The name of the antigen, Date of the operation, Destination (from /to), Quantities received</li>
<li>Number of the batch</li>
<li>Expiry date of the batch</li>
<li>Balance in stock</li>
<li>Remarks</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-vaccine-physical-stock-taking">4. Vaccine physical stock taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-vaccine-physical-stock-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Means making a total count of quantities of vaccines in stock.</li>
<li>Should cover all vaccines stores and should be carried out every month before ordering the supply.</li>
<li>The stocks balance should be adjusted according to the physical stocks done.</li>
<li>If the actual quantity is more than the theoretical stock, the difference should be recorded in the vaccine stock ledger and the remarks written as extra doses</li>
<li>If the actual quantity is less than the theoretical stock, the difference should be recorded under as remarks written as missing doses.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Importance; Planning for annual target setting</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Ordering of new stock</li>
<li>Detect expired-minimizing wastage</li>
<li>Detect lost potency- minimizing wastage.</li>
<li>Monthly reporting on consumption</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Temp Monitoring chart- morning and evening readings.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaccine-storage-and-management">VACCINE STORAGE AND MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccine-storage-and-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="vaccines-forecasting">Vaccines Forecasting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaccines-forecasting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>In order to accurately estimate the vaccines, reliable data must be collected from the health facilities to the S counties.</li>
<li>Having set the target number of children to be vaccinated in the new-year, each health facility should forecast the no. of doses of vaccines required to reach all the target children and WRA.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-obtaining-accurate-forecasting-of-vaccine-needs">Advantages of obtaining accurate forecasting of vaccine needs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-obtaining-accurate-forecasting-of-vaccine-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It leads to efficient management of vaccines and immunization sessions</li>
<li>It eliminates shortages or overstocking of vaccines</li>
<li>It improves vaccine use and reduction of wastages</li>
<li>It helps to monitor the progress of immunization in relation to target coverage</li>
</ol>
<p>There are three methods commonly used to estimate vaccine needs:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Target population</li>
<li>Previous consumption</li>
<li>Size of immunization sessions</li>
</ol>
<p>All facilities are required to estimate vaccine needs using the target population method and if the Health facilities are sharing the same population, previous consumption method would be suitable.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="target-population-method">Target Population Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#target-population-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Target popn is the number of children &lt;1 yr &amp; women of childbearing age (15-49 years old).</p>
<p>To estimate target population a number of parameter are necessary, which are:</p>
<p>a. Target population
b. Immunisation schedule.
c. Immunisation coverage target
d. Wastage rate and wastage factor</p>
<ul>
<li>The national policy is to reach every child in the subcounty..</li>
<li>The Immunization coverage target for each antigen is depends on the health facility and district micro plans and work plans respectively.</li>
<li>These plans indicate the attainable percentage coverage at the end of current year.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="essential-immunization-supplies">Essential Immunization Supplies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#essential-immunization-supplies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>DVI will continue to supply government prescribed childhood and adult vaccines, non-reusable injection devices, safety boxes, monitoring tools, gas and gas cylinders, IEC materials, cold chain equipment and spare parts to all public and government supported immunizing health facilities and those run by other organizations.</p>
<p>Facilities, Districts and Counties are encouraged to supplement the supply of liquid petroleum gas, gas cylinders and refrigeration equipment through other sources of funding but in line with specifications provided by DVI.</p>
<p>All other vaccines outside the government prescribed schedules such as MMR, hepatitis A, Meningococcal, varicella, seasonal influenza vaccines must be licensed for use by the Pharmacy and Poisons Board and conform to the Kenya National drug policy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="distribution-of-vaccination-logistics">Distribution of Vaccination Logistics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#distribution-of-vaccination-logistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Division of Vaccines &amp; Immunization in collaboration with the Kenya Medical Supplies Agency (KEMSA) shall be responsible for the receipt, storage and distribution of the government vaccination supplies/equipment to the districts and counties.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arranging-equipment-and-materials-at-the-immunization-station">Arranging equipment and materials at the immunization station<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arranging-equipment-and-materials-at-the-immunization-station" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You need a table to arrange the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>A vaccine carrier in which to place vaccines and keep them cold;</li>
<li>Foam pads on top of the ice packs in the vaccine carrier to keep the vaccines cold.</li>
<li>Adequate doses of vaccines.</li>
<li>Auto-Disable syringes Reconstitution syringes and needles.</li>
<li>Dry cotton swabs in galipot or clean container.</li>
<li>Tally sheet and summary sheets.</li>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklets and the TT cards.</li>
<li>Permanent child registers and TT register.</li>
<li>AEFI form.</li>
<li>Near the table you should have Safety box for disposing used syringes &amp; needles and refuse bins.</li>
<li>A source of clean running water, soap, and disposable hand-drying materials.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="points-to-remember-in-mch">Points to remember in MCH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-remember-in-mch" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep vaccines cold in a refrigerator and maintain +2°C to +8°C.</li>
</ul>
<p>Keep the refrigerator closed all the time</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Take out from refrigerator all vaccines you will need for the session and put them in a vaccine carrier</li>
<li>Ensure that the vaccine carriers are closed all the time.</li>
<li>Change the ice pack before temperature reach +8°C</li>
<li>Be friendly to both the parents/guardians and children</li>
<li>Check all children to see what immunizations they have had and what they are due for</li>
<li>If in doubt, ask the parents/guardians and confirm from the card. Look for presence of BCG scar</li>
<li>Give immunizations to all children, even the sick ones, unless the child needs hospitalisation</li>
<li>Remind the clinical officer/nurse to send sick children to you for immunization</li>
<li>Check the time interval between doses or immunization. For DPT-HepB+Hib and OPV, Do not give second and third doses if the time interval is less than 4 weeks</li>
<li>REMEMBER: Do not give birth dose of oral Polio after two (2 weeks). To avoid giving different return dates for DPT-HepB+Hib, OPV and PCV10.</li>
</ul>
<p>At subsequent visits, start both antigens at six (6 weeks) and repeat at interval of 4 weeks.</p>
<ul>
<li>On the other hand, even if the time limit is long past the minimum interval of 4 weeks give the next dose</li>
<li>Do not start the schedule again. E.g. if you see a child who had first dose DPT-HepB+Hib, PCV and OPV six months ago, give second dose DPT-HepB+Hib, PCV and OPV</li>
<li>Mark on the tally sheet accordingly after each immunization you give.</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember to put down the date of immunization.</p>
<p>Fill in the mother and child card properly as required</p>
<ul>
<li>Make sure you explain clearly to the mother when to come for the next dose or the next immunization even if her child is sick.</li>
<li>Tell mothers about the reaction to expect from immunizations to dispel rumours.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reassure and tell them what to expect and how to respond.</p>
<ul>
<li>Remember: Injectable immunizations need sterile procedures.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ensure your equipments i.e. AD syringes, reconstitution syringes and safety boxes are available and properly assembled.</p>
<ul>
<li>USE ONLY ONE STERILE SYRINGE AND NEEDLE FOR EACH INJECTION.</li>
</ul>
<p>After use, dispose it into safety box immediately at the point of use.</p>
<ul>
<li>After the clinic session, take all tally sheets and fill in the monthly summary sheet.</li>
</ul>
<p>Clean and tidy up the clinic before you go off duty, ready for the next day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-service-delivery-strategies">Immunization Service delivery strategies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-service-delivery-strategies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Static /fixed - non mobile SDP offering day-day immunization services eg H/facilities.</li>
<li>Outreach services</li>
</ol>
<p>where you take MCH services and curative services from a health facility</p>
<p>to the community within the catchment area and return back to the health facility the same day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scheduling-days-and-times-for-outreach-sessions">Scheduling days and times for outreach sessions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scheduling-days-and-times-for-outreach-sessions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>At least once in a month; the multi-dose vaccines DPT-HepB+Hib, OPV and Tetanus Toxoid require an interval of at least a month between doses.</li>
</ul>
<p>Activities involved in an outreach or mobile clinic include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Determine the need for outreach clinics in terms of access and utilization</li>
<li>Determining the size of target population and the number of children and women that you can immunize in one session</li>
<li>For the best results, consult with community leaders and clients about dates and time, as they will help mobilize the community.</li>
<li>Discuss your plans for mobile/outreach clinics with the members of the SCHMT-support.</li>
<li>Make sure you tell mothers which days to expect you, and the time session will start. Be reliable and punctual.</li>
<li>Make sure that you keep vaccines cold (+2°C to +8°C degrees Centigrade).</li>
<li>When you arrive, arrange your mobile or outreach clinics similar to that of your static H/facility.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Once the immunization session starts, open your cold box or vaccine carrier once, take the vaccines you need according to the number of mothers and children expected and put them on holes in the sponge which is replaced on vaccine carrier during the session, replace ice packs as soon as the ice has melted. Carry a spare vaccine carrier/cold box with icepacks for replacement.</li>
<li>Complete the immunization tally sheet and remember to transfer the data and the name of the outreach clinic to the immunization summary sheet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="completing-an-outreach-session">Completing an outreach session<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#completing-an-outreach-session" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Repacking the vaccine carrier</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Note the temperature inside the vaccine carrier at the end of the session.
If the temperature is &gt;+8°C, Vaccines be discarded unless VVM shows that it is still safe for use.
Pack unopened vaccines and open vials for which multi-dose vial policy is applicable.</li>
<li>Put empty vials to be discarded in a separate container be carried back to facility for proper disposal.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Leave outreach site tidy</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Do not leave behind anything that might be a health risk to the community.</li>
<li>Collect safety boxes containing sharps and take the safety boxes back to the facility.
Do not leave any syringes and needles at the site.</li>
<li>The health worker should supervise the burning of other wastes on site.</li>
<li>Do not leave any empty or glass vials at the site.
Return tables, chairs and other equipments to the owners.</li>
<li>Thank the local people who have helped to organise the session &amp; remind them when you will return.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>At the facility
Return vaccines to the refrigerator:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>If the ice packs in your vaccine carrier have melted during your trip back to the health facility and temperature is above +8°C, and VVM has not reached discard point.
Return the vaccines in the refrigerator and indicate use first so that they will be used first during the next session.</li>
<li>Put ice – packs into the freezer, check and record the temperature.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-a-mobile-clinic">3. A mobile clinic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-a-mobile-clinic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>taking MCH services to a community, lasting for more than a day without returning to the health facility.</p>
<p>An outreach immunization session is held in a location where the health workers can go out and return the facility the same day.</p>
<p>They are held periodically, at interval of one, two or three months.</p>
<p>For success outreach sessions in a community should be held in the same place (for example school), on the same day of the week and at the same time, to maximise the likelihood that people will remember to attend.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-supplemental-immunization-activities-emergency-campaigns-an-opportunity-for-the-community-outreach-and-education-about-immunizations-and-preventable-diseases-respectively-done-during-an-epidemic-eg-measles-poliomyelitis-diseases-or-aefis-in-the-community-to-allay-anxiety-social-mobilization-required-by-use-of-media-community-barazas-to-mobilize-the-community">4. supplemental immunization activities-( emergency campaigns)-An opportunity for the community outreach and education about immunizations and preventable diseases respectively. done during an epidemic eg measles, poliomyelitis diseases or AEFIs in the community to allay anxiety. Social mobilization required by use of media, community barazas to mobilize the community.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-supplemental-immunization-activities-emergency-campaigns-an-opportunity-for-the-community-outreach-and-education-about-immunizations-and-preventable-diseases-respectively-done-during-an-epidemic-eg-measles-poliomyelitis-diseases-or-aefis-in-the-community-to-allay-anxiety-social-mobilization-required-by-use-of-media-community-barazas-to-mobilize-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-integration-strategy-mother-child-care-both-are-served-under-one-roof-at-the-same-time">5. Integration strategy (Mother child care)-both are served under one roof at the same time.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-integration-strategy-mother-child-care-both-are-served-under-one-roof-at-the-same-time" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Services in MCH include-growth monitoring, Rx of minor ailments, PNC, ANC, Immunization, record keeping, counseling, Hx taking-BCG scar formation</p>
<p>Importance-saves time</p>
