<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assign-how-to-initiate-integrated-services-to-include-immunization-in-h-facility">ASSIGN. How to initiate integrated services to include immunization in H/facility.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assign-how-to-initiate-integrated-services-to-include-immunization-in-h-facility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="innovate-approaches-to-immunization">Innovate approaches to immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innovate-approaches-to-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Decade of vaccines approaches;</p>
<ol>
<li>Global vaccine action plan (GVAP) 2011-2020</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Endorsed by 194 member states of WHO assembly in May 2012 to achieve decade of vaccines vision by ensuring universal access to immunization.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aimed at preventing deaths from immunizable diseases esp MDG No.4 reducing child mortality&amp;morbidity.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Incorporated other partners like UNICEF, GAVI alliance, Bill&amp;Melinda Gates Foundation, civil society, Manufacturers, media&amp;private sector in achieving GVAP goals.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Global vaccine action for Pneumonia &amp; diarhoea (GVAPD) integration approach to diarrhoea prevention and control</li>
</ol>
<p>The Plan proposes a cohesive approach to ending preventable diarrhoea deaths by use of rota virus vaccine. It brings together critical services and interventions to create healthy environments, promote practises known to protect children from diseases and ensure that every child has access to proven and appropriate preventive and treatment measures.</p>
<p>In order to achieve this goal, at all levels of the health sector better coordination and integration among programmes that deliver the different interventions is critical. These programmes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Newborn, Child and Adolescent Health Unit (NCAHU),</li>
<li>Nutrition Unit,</li>
<li>Environmental health Unit</li>
<li>relevant Partners</li>
</ul>
<p>REDUCE PNEUMONIA &amp; DIARHEA MORBIDITY AND MORTALITY Exclusive breastfeeding for six months Adequate nutrition Prevent low birth weight Reduce indoor air pollution Hand washing PROTECT children who become ill with pneumonia &amp; Diarrhea Case management in community, health centre and hospital TREAT children becoming ill with pneumonia &amp; Diarrhea Vaccination against Rotavirus, measles, pertussis, Strep pn and Hibb Prevention of HIV in children Cotrimoxazole prophylaxis for HIV -infected and exposed children Zinc supplementation for children with diarrhoea PREVENT Children by providing a healthy environment</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reach-every-district-red-or-child-approach">Reach Every District (RED) or Child Approach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reach-every-district-red-or-child-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>WHO &amp; other partners strategy to increase immunization coverage by reaching every child in the district mostly in Africa.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foccuses on planning, managing &amp; monitoring H/services to improve immunization coverage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The pri implementation level is the district.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aimed at empowering districts to plan, implement &amp; monitor own immunization services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Promotes partnerships btn districts, H/workers &amp; communities to improve popn access &amp; utilization services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continuity use of program data to monitor progress &amp; solve problems.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="red-approach-operational-components">RED approach operational components<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#red-approach-operational-components" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Effective planning strategies for better resource mx;human, finance&amp;material to achieve immunization targets.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reaching all target popns eg &lt;1yr, WRA (pregnant) plus ;underimmunized, unimmunized, unreached or hard to reach by outreach/mobile clinics to offer immunization services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide supportive supervision to identify gaps including OJT/ training needs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community linkages to increase immunization coverage by social mobilization-comm/dialogue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring &amp; Evaluation for action by utilization of data generated to identify and solve problems.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Role of WHO &amp; partners in RED approach</p>
<ul>
<li>Set norms &amp; standards supporting member states in implementation of RED approach</li>
<li>Mobilizing additional resources for implementation of RED approach.</li>
<li>Advocating with govnts &amp; partners to embrace RED approach.</li>
<li>M&amp;E routine immunization activities in the region.</li>
</ul>
<p>Accomplishments of RED approach</p>
<ul>
<li>Implemented almost in all countries.</li>
<li>90% of 17 countries reported immunization coverage target of Pentavalent.</li>
<li>Hep B&amp;HiB vaccines introduced to routine immunization schedule.</li>
<li>Financial support to countries in implementing RED approach.</li>
</ul>
<p>Challenges in implementation of RED approach</p>
<ul>
<li>Lack of govnt collaboration at national, county &amp; Scounty levels.</li>
<li>Insufficient funding for RED approach</li>
<li>Lack of enough qualified trained staff to implement RED Approach.</li>
<li>Inadequate resources like equipment with proper tools and spare parts.</li>
<li>Program shortfalls like lack of staff motivation leads to poor service delivery.</li>
</ul>
<p>New challenges to immunization</p>
<p>Unimmunized - eligible child for immunization but not received any antigen.</p>
<p>Under immunized (drop out) - eligible child for immunization who hasn't completed vaccines</p>
<p>Unreached - Has never been immunized due to lack of social mobilization.</p>
<p>Hard to reach - geographically unable to access immunization services. Compassable roads.</p>
<p>INFCTION PRACTICES IN IMMUNIZATION</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Handwashing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aseptic technique in administration of MDVV, swabbing inj site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of PPE eg Gloving in case of symptomatic HIV/AIDS disease, Apron, uniform etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensuring safe injection?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>A safe injection is one that does not harm the recipient, health worker &amp; the community to any risk.</p>
<p>An injection is considered safe for:</p>
<ul>
<li>The mother or child, when a health worker uses a sterile syringe and a sterile needle and appropriate injection technique;</li>
<li>The health worker, when he or she avoids needle-stick injuries; and</li>
<li>Community, when waste created as a result of used injection equipment is disposed of correctly and does not cause harmful levels of pollution and injuries</li>
</ul>
<p>What Is unsafe injection</p>
<p>One that can result in transmission from one patient to another such infectious</p>
<p>Complications as HIV/AIDS, Hepatitis B and C and D.</p>
<p>Transmission from patient to health worker has also been reported in some health care settings.</p>
<p>Some common injection practices that can cause harm to the recipient</p>
<ul>
<li>Re-using a syringe or needle.</li>
<li>Changing needle but re-using syringe.</li>
<li>Loading syringe with multiple antigens and injecting multiple persons.</li>
<li>Leaving needle on the vial for withdrawal of additional doses.</li>
<li>Touching sterile parts of syringe and needle.</li>
<li>Applying pressure to bleeding injection site with used materials or dirty fingers.</li>
<li>Keeping freeze-dried vaccines for more than 6 hours after reconstitution.</li>
<li>Mixing two partial opened vaccines to constitute a dose.</li>
<li>Storing medications and vaccines in the same stage.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="practices-that-can-harm-health-worker">Practices that can harm Health worker<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#practices-that-can-harm-health-worker" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Recapping.</li>
<li>Placing used needles on surfaces or carrying them from point of use for disposal at a designated area.</li>
<li>Sorting out mixed health care wastes.</li>
<li>Using injection equipment for non-injection purposes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="practices-that-harm-the-community">Practices that harm the community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#practices-that-harm-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Leaving used syringes and needle in unprotected areas where they can be easily accessible to children and grazing animals.</li>
<li>Community can also be at risk when injection equipment is carelessly disposed of and because of its commercial value, it can be retrieved, resold and reused.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-aimed-at-promoting-injection-safety">STEPS AIMED AT PROMOTING INJECTION SAFETY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-aimed-at-promoting-injection-safety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Minimize the risk of needle-stick injuries</li>
<li>Pre-filled AD injection devices</li>
<li>One syringe one child injection</li>
<li>Swabbing site of injection</li>
<li>Proper needle/syringe disposal-safety box</li>
<li>Avoid recapping of needles</li>
<li>Give the right vaccine safely</li>
<li>Hand Washing for IP.</li>
<li>Positioning the child correctly before an administering an injection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="handling-syringes-and-needles-safely">Handling syringes and needles safely<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#handling-syringes-and-needles-safely" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You have to hold a syringe to give an injection, but should not touch part that comes into contact with the vaccine or the child.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="do-not-touch">Do not touch:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-not-touch" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The shaft of the needle;</li>
<li>The bevel of the needle;</li>
<li>The adaptor of the needle;</li>
<li>The adaptor of the syringe; and</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-23108982.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg">
Figure 4B: Parts of a syringe and needle that must not be touched</p>
<p>IMPORTANT: If you touch any of these parts, discard the syringe and needle and get new sterile ones.</p>
<p>The plunger seal of the syringe.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunization-work-area-to-minimize-risk-of-injury">Immunization work area to minimize risk of injury:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-work-area-to-minimize-risk-of-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health workers should plan the layout of their work-place ensure that:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Vaccine carrier is in a safe and cool area;</li>
<li>Tally sheets can be easily used;</li>
<li>Person administering vaccine is between the child and the injection sharps or safety box;</li>
<li>Health workers dispose used needles at point of use without moving too far;</li>
<li>Each injection area to have its own safety box;</li>
<li>Have the mother sit and place the child on her lap. Make sure one of the mother’s arms is behind the child’s back, and one of the child’s arms wraps around the mother’s side.</li>
<li>The mother may tuck the child’s legs btn her own to secure them, or she may hold the child’s legs.</li>
<li>H/Worker should avoid holding the child as they require using both hands to administer the injection;</li>
<li>Always tell the mother when you are about to give the injection;</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-waste-management-segregation">5. Waste Management/segregation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-waste-management-segregation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Waste are materials or products made useless for any further use e.g. used syringes and needles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terminologies-used-in-waste-management">Terminologies used in waste management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies-used-in-waste-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Segregation of waste: separation of wastes at points of generation into different and distinct containers or bags according to national colour codes.</p>
<p>Segregation should be separated into harmful (hazardous) and non-hazardous waste.</p>
<p>Proper waste segregation should be able to minimize hazardous waste requiring special handling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="colour-coding">Colour coding:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#colour-coding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Yellow bag---for hazardous wastes</p>
<p>Black bag--- Non-hazardous wastes</p>
<p>Red bag---Infectious wastes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-safety-box">6. Safety Box:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-safety-box" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A leak and puncture proof container that carries 100 syringes and needles when <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>3</mn><mn>4</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{3}{4}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">4</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> full.</li>
<li>Should NOT full level to avoid spillage, needle stick injuries and to easy the sealing of safety box and should be stored safely awaiting transportation to the central disposal site.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safety-box-precautions">Safety Box Precautions.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safety-box-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do not open used safety boxes or emptied for Re-use.</li>
<li>Do not squeeze or force syringes inside the safety box.</li>
<li>Sharps should be disposed into the safety boxes immediately at point of use.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-safe-waste-disposal-methods">7. Safe waste disposal methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-safe-waste-disposal-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incinerator: This is a structure constructed of bricks for the burning of wastes. There are a number of models of incinerators available in the market.</p>
<p>They are De Monfort, SICIM and Medicin 400 which uses gas as source of fuel.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incineration">Incineration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incineration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>completely destroys needles and syringes by burning at temperatures above <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>800</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">800^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">80</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The high temperature kills microorganisms and reduces the volume of waste to a minimum and produces less air pollution than opening burning.</p>
<p>Some hospitals incinerate on-site while others transport waste to a central incineration area in the district/division.</p>
<p>Burning in a metal drum (container burning) if no incinerator is available or burning in a protected hearth is another way to dispose of used injection equipment and contaminated needles.</p>
<p>Burying of wastes eg sharps deep into the soil</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Decontamination of immunization equipment-decontaminant eg jik. Process</li>
<li>Sterilization of the immunization equipment.</li>
<li>Daily cleaning of the immunization area eg dump dusting</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="data-management-monitoring-and-evaluation">DATA MANAGEMENT, MONITORING AND EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#data-management-monitoring-and-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-terms">Definition of terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Monitoring:</strong> Systematic and continuous process of examining processes, procedures &amp; practices within a program.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is day to day activities within a program with the aim of identifying problems and developing solutions to those. (inputs)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Data is collected, analyzed, reported &amp; used routinely as defined by the program.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Evaluation:</strong> this is a periodic assessment of the overall program performance. (Outputs)</p>
<ul>
<li>Aims to measure the program performance against its objective at specific times.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Performance:</strong> level of fulfillment of operational capacity of a person or a program.</p>
<p><strong>Activity:</strong> a task or a set of interrelated tasks aimed at generating a product or a result.</p>
<p><strong>Indicators:</strong> this is a variable used to compare program performance against its stated objective(s).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="denominators-targets-of-immunization-coverage">Denominators (targets) of immunization coverage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#denominators-targets-of-immunization-coverage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To be able to conduct monitoring and evaluation process, one must first set the target to be achieved.</p>
<p>Two types of <strong>targets are set</strong> for each facility namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>0-11 months old for (population &lt;1 year old) for primary infant vaccination.</li>
<li>Pregnant women (expected deliveries) for vaccination with tetanus toxoid.</li>
<li>Women of Child Bearing Age (for districts considered at high risk of neonatal tetanus) for vaccination with tetanus toxoid1.</li>
</ul>
<p>At the beginning of each year, each facility must calculate the number of children and women to</p>
<p>be vaccinated with each antigen.</p>
<ul>
<li>This process is facilitated by the SCHMT at a meeting held at the beginning of each year. — During this meeting heads of health facilities bring copies of their facility’s “Immunization and Vitamin A Summary sheet” for the previous year (12 months).</li>
</ul>
<p>The data is then summarized into divisional immunization data for the previous 12 months and facilities within the division are assigned targets for the New Year based on the current year’s divisional population and proportional contribution to the divisional performance during the last 12 months.</p>
<p>Target setting for health facilities is carried out annually during a review meeting organized by the District Health Management Team (DHMT).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supportive-supervision">Supportive supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supportive-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Def:</strong> Facilitative approach promoting mentorship in joint problem solving &amp; communication btn supervisors and surpervisee.</p>
<ul>
<li>Aimed at improving routine program immunization by close M&amp;E by ensuring staff personal&amp;CPD.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supervision-styles">Supervision styles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervision-styles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Autocratic or authoritarian</strong>—decision is by the supervisor</p>
<p><strong>Laisser Faire</strong>—do what you want</p>
<p><strong>Democratic</strong>—both surpivisor and surpervisee decide what to do.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-supportive-supervision">Importance of supportive supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-supportive-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Training needs by identification gaps in skills delivery</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>-Developing better interpersonal skills/relationship.
-Communication btn surpervisor &amp;surpervisee
-Skill development by OJT mentorship eg CT.
-Corrective action in case of AEFIs to allay community anxiety.
-Conflict resolution eg staff arrest or indiscipline.
-Increase confidence of H/Service providers.
-Reduce stress due to burn out.
-Offers opportunities to reflect &amp;link knowledge &amp;practice.</p>
<p>Supervision Areas: Vaccine stocks/accessories/logistics, cold chain system/equipment, communication and advocacy (H/education), performance indicators/ documentation, Emergency preparedness eg AEFIs/Equipment, IP practices (waste mx, Injection Safety) &amp;HR(skills)-training needs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-epi-manager">Role of EPI Manager<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-epi-manager" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assign-role-of-chw-in-immunization">Assign: Role of CHW in immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assign-role-of-chw-in-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-communication-for-immunization">IMPORTANCE OF COMMUNICATION FOR IMMUNIZATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-communication-for-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>creates awareness (access), acceptance, trust, and utilization these services hence raising&amp;Sustaining immunization coverage for the target groups &amp;reduces the vaccine preventable diseases.</li>
<li>To achieve higher coverage and a significant reduction of drop-out rates,</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="messages-and-communication-channels-health-education">MESSAGES AND COMMUNICATION CHANNELS (HEALTH EDUCATION)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#messages-and-communication-channels-health-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>priority messages for immunization:</p>
<ul>
<li>Importance of immunization; why immunize a child?</li>
<li>The diseases children are protected against after immunization</li>
<li>Importance of completing the schedule on time and the consequences of not doing so</li>
<li>Side-effects and what to do about them</li>
<li>The need to immunize even sick children when they are due</li>
<li>The need to immunize against measles despite history of measles infection</li>
<li>The importance of the Child Health Card</li>
<li>Community participation for mobilization for immunization</li>
</ul>
<p>Using this information, the following basic messages were developed by KEPI, and should be Complemented by more focused messages with communities and caregivers, based on local situational analysis and pre-testing:</p>
<ul>
<li>All children under 12 months need to be vaccinated against these diseases, i.e. TB, whooping cough, diphtheria, tetanus, measles, poliomyelitis, hepatitis B, Hib, pneumonia, rotavirus, yellow fever.</li>
<li>Children need to get all immunizations at the right time to protect them from these diseases.</li>
<li>Immunization prevents death and disability from the diseases.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>An immunized child is a protected child.</li>
<li>Every healthy child must have an up-to-date immunization card.</li>
<li>Immunizations are free. You can get them at any health facility.</li>
<li>Immunizing your children saves time and money.</li>
<li>Investing in immunization is a priority for Kenya.</li>
</ul>
<p>Every child who is due for immunization must be immunized unless severely ill or hospitalized.</p>
<p>Messages should be targeted to particular issues and groups and pre-tested before disseminating.</p>
<p>They should be motivating, persuasive, credible, and action-oriented.</p>
<p>Maximum effort should be made to have free broadcast and press coverage of the improved immunization service.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-participation-in-immunization">Community participation in immunization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-participation-in-immunization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pulling together of community members for decision making towards uptake of immunization services hence promoting own individual, family &amp; community health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="importance">Importance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="assign-challenges-in-community-participation">Assign; Challenges in community participation.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assign-challenges-in-community-participation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-to-immunization-services">Barriers to immunization services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-to-immunization-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>hinder access or utilization of services.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is important to understand potential barriers to immunization to be able to adapt services and design community and communication interventions appropriately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-faced-by-the-immunization-programme">Barriers faced by the immunization programme<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-faced-by-the-immunization-programme" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Access/Distance to services (rural and/or remote communities with no/irregular outreach)</li>
<li>stock outs (Unavailability of supplies/vaccines)</li>
<li>Poor health worker knowledge and training</li>
<li>Poor service quality and reliability</li>
<li>Lack of antenatal/perinatal care</li>
<li>Missed opportunities (including not having vaccination card at the time of the clinic visit, vaccinator absent at the designated time of immunization services, and children receiving curative services only (i.e. the child’s immunization status is not assessed))</li>
<li>Lack of communication by H/service provider.</li>
<li>Living in urban area (duration of travel time in an urban setting)</li>
<li>Living in settlement/slum area</li>
<li>Lack of physician referral to services</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Cost of vaccinations</li>
<li>Poor timing/availability of vaccinators</li>
<li>Vaccination schedule</li>
<li>Weak and inadequate supervision at the local and district level</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-related-communication-information-system">Barriers related Communication &amp; information system.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-related-communication-information-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lack of health educators</li>
<li>Poor communication from health worker (perceived provider rudeness or a lack of trust in him/her)</li>
<li>Lack of information on vaccination schedule, when child is due, where to receive vaccinations</li>
<li>Inadequate media messages</li>
<li>Dissemination of inadequate or incorrect information by health care worker</li>
<li>Lack of media exposure</li>
<li>Lack of community involvement</li>
<li>Gender of health worker</li>
<li>Lack of trust or social connections</li>
<li>Lack of home visits by health worker</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-societal-xetics">Family &amp; societal xetics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-societal-xetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Illiterate caregivers</li>
<li>Ignorance-Low education level of caregivers</li>
<li>Poverty-Low socioeconomic status</li>
<li>Living in a large family/having older siblings</li>
<li>Belonging to minority group</li>
<li>Migrants-rural-urban</li>
<li>Blue collar worker/occupation</li>
<li>Marital status – mom unmarried</li>
<li>Male headed household</li>
<li>Mother's age</li>
<li>Other domestic issues (conflict/death)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="parental-attitudes">Parental attitudes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parental-attitudes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Caregivers' lack of knowledge about immunizations</li>
<li>Motivation</li>
<li>No understanding of vaccine importance (Caregivers frequently not aware of the need to vaccinate their child or the threat of disease transmission if their child was not vaccinated).</li>
<li>No information on when to vaccinate</li>
<li>Misconception of vaccinations (ranging from the impression that vaccinations do not work to the concerns that vaccinations harm the child, or cause disease or other adverse event such as sterility).</li>
<li>Fear of side effects</li>
<li>Fear of vaccination</li>
<li>Being female child</li>
<li>Religious/cultural/traditional beliefs against vaccines</li>
<li>Lack of family discussions of immunization services.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="addressing-barriers-to-immunization-and-ensuring-service-delivery-and-utilization">Addressing barriers to immunization and ensuring service delivery and utilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#addressing-barriers-to-immunization-and-ensuring-service-delivery-and-utilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Utilize your immunization coverage data (registers, monitoring charts, tally sheets, etc.) and other</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>study data (e.g. KAP, focus groups, programme reviews) to determine where you have access (low penta1) and/or utilization (low penta3) problems. Refer to Chapter 9 on how to analyse and use these data. Based on this analysis, you should determine which barriers apply to your programme,\update your microplan, and adapt your services to address these barriers, in collaboration with the community.</p>
<p>Although barriers will vary and your strategy should be adapted based on the situation at your facility, following are some possible suggestions to maximize availability and utilization of services:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lack-of-time-to-come-for-services">Lack of time to come for services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lack-of-time-to-come-for-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Timing of session might be improper: avoid closing the MCH clinics in the afternoons. Remember immunization services are from Monday to Friday 8 am to 5 pm.</li>
<li>Avoid (or choose) market days, depending on the suitability within the locality.</li>
<li>If you plan a weekly session or a monthly outreach session, come on the same day at the same time: it will be easier for everybody to remember (and if this needs to be adjusted, plan with the community and communicate any changes well in advance – if you miss sessions, community confidence will reduce)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="problems-of-distance-and-transportation">Problems of distance and transportation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problems-of-distance-and-transportation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If the distance is greater than 5 km, plan advance or outreach strategies and communicate the dates, locations, and times beforehand. Be sure that these sessions are not missed or that if there are delays or rescheduling, communities are notified promptly. (Failure to conduct outreach as planned will result in drop-outs and lower coverage.)</li>
<li>If mothers have major problems of transportation, be sure not to miss any opportunity to immunize a child. They might not be able to come back another time. Reorganize outreach sessions, planned with the communities, to hold them closer to the community on the appropriate days/times.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="long-waiting-time">Long waiting time<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-waiting-time" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If immunization is offered daily, from 8 am to 5 pm, waiting time will be decreased.</li>
<li>Follow a first come, first serve basis to reduce waiting time (and do not wait for quorum to begin vaccinating).</li>
<li>Make this waiting time both pleasant (by providing shade, seats, fresh water) and useful (by giving health education).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="attitude-of-staff">Attitude of staff<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attitude-of-staff" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Be polite and friendly, even if you are tired.</li>
<li>Remember, immunization decreases diseases and thus decreases your work, so do not be impatient with caregivers.</li>
<li>Immunize daily from 8 a.m. to 5 p.m., you will have fewer children at a time and this will give you more time to talk to the mothers.</li>
<li>Seek the help of community members.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lack-of-organisation-of-services">Lack of organisation of services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lack-of-organisation-of-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Address service delivery problems (and seek assistance from communities, if needed): Ensure adequate stock of vaccines and injection material, be sure equipment is in working order and fix broken equipment, ensure supply of gas and transport, conduct fixed and outreach sessions as planned, utilize monitoring tools (including availability of Mother and Child Health Booklets).</li>
<li>Mother not told to return for subsequent dose: always give a return date and write it in the Mother and Child Health Booklet and confirm with her that she understands.</li>
<li>No card provided by the mother; don't send her away. According to the child's age and the mother's memory, you should still vaccinate and record it on a piece of paper. Remember, an extra dose of vaccine will not do harm. A missed opportunity might make the child at risk of these diseases. Remind the mother to keep and protect the Mother and Child Health Booklet and</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="negative-attitudes-and-beliefs">Negative attitudes and beliefs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#negative-attitudes-and-beliefs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Identify traditional beliefs which are against or question immunization or health services and negotiate with the traditional and other leaders to change attitudes and ensure acceptance of services.</p>
<ul>
<li>Where people are not convinced that immunization protects the child or mother, health workers should explain the greater risk of contracting and spreading these diseases and becoming sick or dying if the child or mother is unimmunized.</li>
<li>Negative attitudes of head of village or family should be handled through dialogue with them involving convinced heads, friends or groups.</li>
<li>Negative attitudes of health workers towards the immunization programme and clients should be discussed; try to come up with a positive approach with individuals and at meetings.</li>
<li>Negative attitudes of traditional practitioners can be solved by enlisting their support and ducating them.</li>
<li>Organise seminars/workshops with local leaders and invite them to participate and contribute towards achieving better health for the people.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="missed-opportunities">Missed Opportunities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#missed-opportunities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A missed opportunity for immunization occurs when any eligible child or woman comes to a health facility and does not receive any or all of the vaccine doses for which he or she is eligible.</p>
<p>The opportunity to immunize eligible children is missed when the:</p>
<ul>
<li>Health facility does not offer immunization services</li>
<li>Health facility is experiencing vaccine stock-out</li>
<li>Health workers do not use appropriate contraindications to immunizations</li>
<li>Health workers do not routinely screen children and women for their immunization status and offer the recommended vaccines</li>
<li>Health workers do not give all the vaccines for which the children and women are eligible at the time of the visit.</li>
<li>Health worker decides to schedule certain vaccines for fear of running out of vaccines or a high vaccine wastage (multi-dose lyophilised vaccines)</li>
</ul>
<p>Missed opportunity surveys or rapid situational assessments provide health workers with information that may be used to reduce the number of missed opportunities and increase the number of people</p>
<p>Ways to reduce missed opportunities:</p>
<ul>
<li>Conduct periodic surveys to measure missed opportunities</li>
<li>Identify missed opportunities by examining health facility records and immunization cards (Child Health and Antenatal Cards)</li>
<li>Check immunization status of every child 0-23 months and pregnant women visiting health facilities or coming to the outreach site for any reason. Those in need should be immunized before leaving</li>
<li>Avoid false contraindications to immunization e.g. fever, cold, diarrhoea, vomiting and malnutrition. Incorrect use of contraindications denies life-saving immunizations to many infants</li>
<li>Ensure that all eligible women and children have an immunization card and that they bring the card to every clinic visit and that these cards are checked by the health worker on every visit and the relevant details discussed with the mother</li>
<li>Ensure that those sick enough to be admitted are immunized on admission or before discharge from hospitals</li>
<li>Avoid scheduling of vaccination services and inconsistent outreaches</li>
<li>Encourage health workers to open a multi-dose vial of a lyophilised vaccine, even for one child.</li>
</ul>
<p>Routine immunization indicators</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Variables used to compare performance in terms of efficiency-time, effectiveness-cost and results. They are used to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Convert raw data into useful information</li>
<li>Mark progress towards defined targets</li>
<li>Describe the situation and measure changes over time.</li>
<li>Provide information about a broad range of conditions through a single measure</li>
<li>Enable comparisons between different facilities.</li>
</ul>
<p>A target is an indicator that represents a specific objective to be achieved over a specific period of time</p>
<p>Indicators used in routine immunization are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immunization coverage</li>
<li>Dropout rates</li>
<li>Completeness</li>
<li>Timeliness of reports</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Immunization Coverage:
This is a measure of the extent to which the services being rendered cover the potential need for these services in the community.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunization coverage is the proportion of vaccinated individuals among the target popn. It is one of the most important indicators of a successful immunization programme.</p>
<p>Coverage is calculated by dividing the number of individuals vaccinated with a particular antigen (numerator) by the number of individuals targeted for vaccination with the antigen (denominator) within the same period.</p>
<p>This proportion is then multiplied by 100 to get percentage coverage.</p>
<p>Coverage formula:
(Number of individuals vaccinated) divided by (Number of individuals targeted for vaccination) X 100</p>
<p>The following coverage's are routinely calculated</p>
<ul>
<li>Coverage for each vaccine dose.</li>
<li>Coverage for fully immunized child (Measles 1)</li>
<li>TT2+ coverage</li>
</ul>
<p>Example: During the previous year, health facilities in the Langalanga H/Centre of Nakuru County administered 102 doses of DPT-HepB+HiB3 and 73 doses of measles vaccine to children less than one year of age against target population of 150 children'</p>
<p>Calculate immunization coverage for pentavalent 3 and measles.
DTP3 coverage = 102 divide by 150 X 100 = 68%</p>
<p>The measles immunization coverage is calculated in a similar way.
Measles coverage = 73 divide by 150 X 100 = 49%</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Dropout Rates (DOR):
The number of individuals who start an immunization schedule but fail to get the last dose/antigen on the schedule.</li>
</ol>
<p>For example if a woman brings her child for DPT-Hep-B+Hib1 and OPV1 but does not return for other childhood immunization, her child is considered a "DROP OUT".</p>
<p>Drop out is calculated by subtracting the number of individuals who complete receive the last dose/antigen in the schedule (numerator) and dividing the difference by the number of individuals who started the schedule.</p>
<p>For calculating drop out, pentavalent 1 is considered the first vaccine on the schedule and pentavalent 3 the last vaccine dose.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Dropout rate for measles (measles-pengtavalent1) may also be calculated but the information Should be interpreted differently form dropout for pentavalent.</p>
<p>Dropout rate formula: (Doses of DTP-HepB+Hib-1 minus Doses of DTP/HepB+Hib-3) x 100</p>
<p>Divided (Doses of DTP/HepB+Hib-1)</p>
<p>Example: During the previous year, Kamwaura Dispensary in Nakuru District administered up to the month of August 91 doses of DTP1, and 76 doses of DTP3 to children less than 1 year of age. The drop-out rate for Kamwaura Dispensary is as follows:</p>
<p>DTP-HepB+Hib-1 - DTP/HepB+Hib-3 drop-out rate = (91-76) X 100 = 16%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-completeness-of-the-reports">3. Completeness of the reports<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-completeness-of-the-reports" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Defined in two different ways depending on the level and function of reporting unit.</p>
<p>i. At a health facility level- means that all required fields in a report have been filled.</p>
<p>How well this is done determines the quality of data being reported.</p>
<p>ii. At district and subsequent levels</p>
<p>Defined as the proportion of reports received.</p>
<p>Calculated by dividing the total number of reports received from the reporting units (numerator) by the total number of reporting units (denominator).</p>
<p>The result is then multiplied by 100 to make it a percentage.</p>
<p>Completeness formula: Total reports received divide by total reporting facilities x 100</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="total-expected-reports">Total expected reports<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#total-expected-reports" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health worker should ensure that all monthly reports are sent to the district.</p>
<p>Non-reporting of late data affects the overall district coverage and, subsequently, the national immunization coverage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="timeliness-of-reporting">Timeliness of reporting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#timeliness-of-reporting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A proportion of reports that are received on time.</p>
<p>It is the number of reports received on time divided (numerator) by the total number of reports expected for the period (denominator)</p>
<p>Formula for timeliness: Total reports received on time divide by total reports expected x 100</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Data collected from the tally sheets needs to be summarized, for action at health facility level and transmitted to the district level by 5th of the following month.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The districts then uploads the data on the DHIS website</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When reports are sent and received on time, the possibility of a prompt and effective response is greater.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Late data should not be ignored; they must be sent to the district level to up-date the existing data set at all levels.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Not reporting late data affects the overall district coverage and, subsequently, the national immunization coverage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Late reports should be sent together with the next monthly report with explanatory note specifying the month of the data.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-for-collecting-routine-immunization-data-monitoring-performance">Tools for collecting routine immunization data /monitoring performance.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-for-collecting-routine-immunization-data-monitoring-performance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All immunizations must be accurately recorded at the h/facility in the ;.</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother and Child Health Booklets</li>
<li>Immunization Permanent Register</li>
<li>Immunization tally sheets including Vitamin A</li>
<li>TT Permanent Register</li>
<li>Immunization and Vitamin A Summary Sheet</li>
<li>Immunization Monitoring Chart</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mother-and-child-health-book">Mother and Child Health Book<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mother-and-child-health-book" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the child's/woman's individual immunization record. It is kept by the caregiver and therefore is the only immunization record that is found in the community. This card is brought to the clinic during each visit.</p>
<p>In addition to the demographic information about the child/woman, the following information is recorded in the card:</p>
<ul>
<li>The type of vaccine and dose number</li>
<li>The date the vaccine was given</li>
<li>The date of the next appointment</li>
<li>Any adverse event that may have occurred during a previous vaccination</li>
<li>An immunization card serves the following purposes</li>
<li>Reminds the caregiver when to return to the clinic</li>
<li>Assists the MCH staff to ascertain the immunization status of the child/woman</li>
<li>Allows continuity of service when the child/woman moves to another area.</li>
<li>During coverage surveys, the card is used to verify immunization status of the child/woman.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunizations-and-vitamin-a-tally-sheet">Immunizations and Vitamin A Tally Sheet<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunizations-and-vitamin-a-tally-sheet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is daily record of immunization activities at a health facility. Each vaccine and dose number is recorded appropriately immediately it is administered. The procedure for filling the immunization tally sheet is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>First write the name of the health institution, the name of the district and the date on which you start the sheet.</li>
<li>For each immunization you perform, strike the printed zero vertically at the correct line, according to the type of immunization given and the age group of the child.</li>
<li>On the last line, "Number of Children Immunized" you strike a zero for each child that has completed the immunization schedule.</li>
</ul>
<p>At the end of each day, draw a vertical line across the paper in front of the last 5 zero batch that you have marked.</p>
<ul>
<li>On the top line, enter the date during which those immunizations were performed.</li>
<li>Continue using this sheet until it is full, or until you expect that entries for the next immunization clinic will exceed the numbers of zeros left.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunization-and-vitamin-a-summary-sheets">Immunization and Vitamin A Summary Sheets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-and-vitamin-a-summary-sheets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An immunization summary sheet is a summary of monthly immunizations given at health facility.</p>
<p>It is completed by summarizing the data from the daily tally sheets for a particular month.</p>
<ul>
<li>Fill in the month and name of the health facility.</li>
<li>Each day, when you finish your MCH clinic, draw a vertical line on the immunization tally sheet and count the number of immunization recorded on the tally sheet.</li>
<li>Enter the totals on the summary sheet.</li>
<li>Each column on the sheet represents 1 day of the month, the first line being the first day of the month up to the last date of the month.</li>
<li>Make sure that you enter the totals from the Immunization Tally Sheet in the correct column; on the day the immunizations were given.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This will make your work easier because your monthly report will be compiled daily.</p>
<ul>
<li>When you have filled in the daily entries for a whole month, sum up each row, and enter the totals on the rows written “total” on the right side of the sheet.</li>
<li>Compare it to your target, present it on a monitoring chart and discuss it with the team.</li>
<li>Send the summary sheet within 5 days after the month ends to the District Public Health Nurse and remember to put the date and your name in the space provided at the bottom. *
*NB. The health worker should ensure that all fields in the Monthly Immunization Summary Sheets are filled appropriately before sending to the district level.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunization-permanent-register">Immunization Permanent Register<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-permanent-register" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the permanent record of individual immunization history at the health facility.</p>
<p>Each row represents a single child while each column represents an antigen.</p>
<p>Detailed instructions on how to complete the permanent register are at the back of the cover page. They are summarized as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>When a child is brought for the first time for immunization, register the child in the large Hard cover (register) provided.</li>
</ul>
<p>For ease of follow-up and easy retrieval of the child’s records, the number appearing in the child’s immunization card should be the same as in the register.</p>
<ul>
<li>Every time the child is presented for immunization, you will record the date and vaccine(s) given in the register under the child’s number.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note the child should appear only once in the register.</p>
<ul>
<li>Once a month, you should go through the register and find the children who should have been immunized that month and were not.</li>
<li>Get in contact with the parents and request that they bring the children to the clinic.</li>
</ul>
<p>The community health worker or a public health technician can do this.</p>
<ul>
<li>It is only by your active follow-up that all children in your catchment area will be fully immunized.</li>
</ul>
<p>At every visit to the health facility, the child should be screened for immunization status and all due vaccines administered. Every antigen given to at every visit should be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Recorded on the Permanent register</li>
<li>Recorded on the Mother and Child Health Booklet</li>
<li>Tallied on the immunization tally sheet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tt-permanent-register">TT Permanent Register<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tt-permanent-register" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Just like the immunization permanent register; this is a permanent record of a woman’s immunization with tetanus toxoid. It is completed as follows;</p>
<ul>
<li>When a pregnant woman visits the health facility for the first time, register her in the hardcover hook (register) provided. For ease of follow-up and easy retrieval of the woman’s records, the number appearing in the register should be the same as the one in the TT or antenatal card.</li>
<li>Each time the expectant mother comes for TT immunization, you will record the date and vaccine given in the register under her number.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note that woman should appear only once in the register.</p>
<ul>
<li>Once a month, you should go through the register and find the pregnant women who should have been immunized that month and were not.</li>
<li>You should get in contact with them and advise them to come for immunization.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB. Each time you administer immunizations, record them in three areas i.e. TT antenatal card, tally sheet and the permanent Register</p>
