<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tracking-systems-to-monitor-defaulters">Tracking systems to monitor defaulters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tracking-systems-to-monitor-defaulters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A child who has failed to turn up for immunization at least 2 weeks after the appointment date. Each facility should compile a list of defaulters once a month and efforts to trace them be made. There are several methods used to track defaulters that can be adopted.</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of permanent registers</li>
<li>Use of immunization diary based on monitoring chart.</li>
<li>Use of tickler cards.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunization-monitoring-chart">Immunization Monitoring Chart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-monitoring-chart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A graphical presentation of a facility’s performance as per specific antigen; penta1/3 measles.</li>
<li>It is plotted monthly using data from the monthly immunization summary sheet.</li>
<li>Cumulative data for selected antigen representing key aspects of the immunization program are plotted and monitored monthly and compared with the targeted coverage.</li>
<li>Required data include: total popn of the catchment area, target popn; no. vaccinated with the specific antigens and number of cases of certain vaccine preventable diseases (surveillance).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fig-8-2-how-to-prepare-immunization-monitor-chart">Fig 8.2 How to prepare Immunization Monitor Chart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fig-8-2-how-to-prepare-immunization-monitor-chart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Write the name of health facility.</li>
<li>Fill in the total population for your catchment area.</li>
<li>Fill in the annual target populations for children below 1 year</li>
<li>Fill in the monthly target populations for immunization by dividing the number of children below one year of age by 12.</li>
<li>Fill in the cumulative monthly targets</li>
<li>At the end of each month, enter the total number of immunizations given then add the present month’s total to the previous cumulative total.</li>
<li>Plot on graph the cumulative totals by marking on the right side of the month column you are recording. Draw a line between the new dot and the previous month’s dot.</li>
<li>Subtract the cumulative total for DTP-HepB+Hib1 from the cumulative total for DTP-HepB+Hib3/Measles.</li>
</ol>
<p>This is the cumulative total number of drop-outs for this period of the year.</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>Calculate the cumulative drop-out rate (DOR).</li>
<li>Enter the number of cases of the target diseases seen in the health facility into the appropriate section of the monitoring chart</li>
<li>If no case was reported enter 0 (zero reporting)</li>
</ol>
<p>Cumulative total: the total number of doses of vaccines given in the current month plus the monthly totals for the previous months.</p>
<p>Example: the cumulative number of DTP-HepB+Hib1 doses given by the end of March is the total number of doses given in January plus the total number given in February plus the total number given in March.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="analysis-and-use-of-data-at-health-facility-level">Analysis and use of data at health facility level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analysis-and-use-of-data-at-health-facility-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>After data has been summarized from the tally sheet to the monthly summary sheet, the information used to identify existing problems at health facility level.</li>
<li>This allows the health facility to determine the causes of each problem and possible solutions.</li>
<li>At a health facility, problems can be categorized a problem of access, utilization or both.</li>
<li>Access is defined as the proportion of children who are reached with immunization services.</li>
<li>It is measured using coverage for pentavalent 1 and can either be describe as good (≥ 80%) or poor (&lt;80%).</li>
<li>Utilization is the ability of a healthy facility to retain the children accessed till they receive the Last dose on the schedule.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is measured using the dropout rate between pentavalent 1 and pentavalent 3 (or measles). It can either be low (&lt;10%) or high (≥10%).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Using the defined cut-off for access and utilization, an algorithm is used to assign the facility to a problem category.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="figure-8-3-epi-access-and-utilization-algorithm">Figure 8.3 EPI access and utilization algorithm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#figure-8-3-epi-access-and-utilization-algorithm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Low coverage (&lt;80%) may be caused by the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Inaccessibility (geographical, other barriers) – in this case the children and women are not reached at all or do not utilize the services</li>
<li>Drop-outs – this group starts immunization but does not return to complete the schedule</li>
<li>Dropout is a major obstacle to achieving KEPI coverage objectives.</li>
<li>To reduce dropout rates, health workers should know the extent of the dropout rate problem in their facility catchment area.</li>
<li>A Dropout rate less than 10% or less demonstrates good utilization of services.</li>
<li>A Dropout rate higher than 10% indicates problem with utilization of services.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is therefore necessary to routinely monitor the trends of coverage and dropout rates in order to ensure timely action aimed at reaching every child.</p>
<ul>
<li>Missed opportunities – in this group children and women have had contact with health worker for any other reason – for example, a woman bringing her child suffering from diarrhoea – but both she &amp; her child were not screened for immunization status and were not immunized by the health worker.</li>
</ul>
<p>HIGH coverage with DTP/HepB+Hib1 (&gt;80%) LOW coverage with DTP/HepB+Hib1 (&lt; 80%)</p>
<p>What proportions of the children have ACCESS to immunization services?</p>
<p>(What is the DTP/HepB+Hib1 coverage?)</p>
<p>What proportions of the children COMPLETE the immunization schedule?</p>
<p>(What are the dropout rates?)</p>
<p>Categorize the problems</p>
<p><strong>Drop-out</strong></p>
<p>rate</p>
<p>&lt; 10%</p>
<p><strong>Drop-out rate</strong></p>
<p>&gt; 10%</p>
<p><strong>Drop-out rate</strong></p>
<p>&gt; 10%</p>
<p><strong>Drop-out</strong></p>
<p>rate</p>
<p>&lt; 10%</p>
<ul>
<li>Drop-out rates are low = good utilization</li>
<li>Coverage is high = Good access</li>
</ul>
<p>NO PROBLEM</p>
<p>CATEGORY 1</p>
<ul>
<li>Drop-out rates are high</li>
</ul>
<p>= poor utilization</p>
<ul>
<li>Coverage is high = Good access</li>
</ul>
<p>PROBLEM</p>
<p>CATEGORY 2</p>
<ul>
<li>Drop-out rates are low = good utilization</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Coverage is low = Poor access</p>
<p>PROBLEM</p>
<p>CATEGORY 3</p>
<p>Drop-out rates are high = poor utilization
Coverage is low = Poor access</p>
<p>PROBLEM</p>
<p>CATEGORY</p>
<ul>
<li>Lack of awareness of immunization services or rejection of vaccination due to socio-cultural reasons.</li>
</ul>
<p>Poor utilization (high dropout) of immunization services may be caused by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Irregular supply of vaccines</li>
<li>High workload for staff</li>
<li>Poor staff attitude</li>
<li>Poor scheduling of immunization sessions.</li>
</ul>
<p>To identify the causes of the problems you should hold discussions with the community and health staff.</p>
<p>For promoting completion of the full immunization schedule, include community members by asking them how the service can be made more accessible to them.</p>
<p>In addition, health staff should discuss why children do not begin or complete the immunization schedule.</p>
<p>Exit interviews and observations during sessions by the supervisor provide important hints too. For each problem, there are many possible solutions.</p>
<p>Examples of solutions include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improved communication with the community</li>
<li>Mobilization of additional resources</li>
<li>Use of other immunization strategies e.g. outreach, local immunization days etc.</li>
<li>Scheduling immunization sessions in consultation with the community</li>
<li>Proper forecasting of the vaccines requirements</li>
</ul>
<p>Standard operating procedures</p>
<p>Each immunizing health facility should observe the following requirements:</p>
<ul>
<li>Calculate and display the its catchment area population</li>
<li>Calculate and display its target population (&lt;1 year)</li>
<li>Display a map for catchment population indicating hard to reach areas &amp; special populations</li>
<li>File and store used tally sheets and summary sheets by month and year for at least 3 years</li>
<li>Send immunization summary reports to the district by 5th of the following month.</li>
<li>Regularly Update the district with late reports</li>
<li>Have an up-to-date immunization monitor chart on displayed on the wall</li>
<li>Have a mechanism in place to track defaulters</li>
<li>Establish linkage with the community</li>
</ul>
<p>Other methods for evaluating immunization programme</p>
<p>Apart the data collected routinely (administrative data), there are other methods used periodically to assess the performance of the immunization program. These are usually conducted by a team with certain expertise and at a pre-determined interval and require a lot of planning and hence they are expensive. The commonest methods used are:</p>
<p>Data Quality Self-Assessment (DQS)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The Data Quality Self-assessment (DQS) is a flexible method used to evaluate different aspects of the immunization monitoring system at district and health facility levels. The DQS aims to determine:</p>
<ul>
<li>The accuracy of reported figures for coverage (i.e. number of immunizations) and for any other immunization system indicator</li>
<li>The quality of any component of the immunization monitoring system</li>
</ul>
<p>The assessment includes a review of data accuracy at different levels and a self-designed questionnaire reviewing monitoring quality issues (e.g. availability of vaccination cards, use of tally sheets, directly-observed recording and reporting practices). Data are then analyzed, with a view to identifying strengths and weaknesses which need to be correct.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immunization-survey">Immunization Survey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunization-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An immunization coverage survey examines a small number of individuals to determine their immunization status. It involves visiting homes, examining immunization records and asking the individual, parent or caretaker about immunizations received.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is done in a systematic way so that only a small sample of homes and individuals need to be surveyed in order to obtain valid results that can be generalized to the larger population. The coverage survey will inform about the following issues.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Infant immunization i.e. how well facilities have met their target for immunizing infants. This is important because if a child does not receive the recommended immunizations as early as possible he/she will not receive the maximum protection from vaccine-preventable diseases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tetanus toxoid immunization for women 1.e whether mothers of infants have been immunized with tetanus toxoid (TT).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reasons for immunization failure i.e. why people do not come or return for immunization.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is important because it will help in finding ways to increase your immunization coverage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A coverage survey can validate the results of routine reports and provide additional information.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An advantage of a coverage survey is that it tells how many people were immunized correctly, as well as how many were immunized by other providers.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>It also can provide important information on true coverage in situations where of target children is not known.</p>
<p>The most famous EPI coverage survey is the 30x7 cluster survey where 30 clusters are systematically selected and 7 eligible children are evaluated for their immunization status.</p>
<p>This gives a total of 210 children in the survey.</p>
<p>There are other variations of the survey but they all use the same principles of cluster survey.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="post-introduction-evaluations">Post-Introduction Evaluations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-introduction-evaluations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a periodic survey to evaluate the impact of introducing a new vaccine on the existing programme.</p>
<p>It involves assessing various aspects of the programme: The main areas assessed include (but not limited to) the following.</p>
<ul>
<li>Pre-implementation Planning and Training</li>
<li>Coverage and Reporting</li>
<li>Cold Chain and Vaccine Management</li>
<li>Waste Management, Injection Safety and AEFI</li>
<li>Health Care Worker (HCW) Knowledge, Monitoring and Supervision</li>
<li>Advocacy Communication and Acceptance</li>
</ul>
<p>Post-introduction evaluation usually involves many agencies and is conducted after at-least 6 months after a new vaccine is int</p>
